## Document Digest: ORGAN_i-vii___sub-ORGANS

I've read the full charter. This is a sophisticated institutional architecture—a system designed to prevent different modes of work from collapsing into or distorting each other. Let me structure my analysis:

* * *

### 1. **Core System Logic**

You've formalized a **multi-mode production ecosystem** with seven primary functions + three supporting backplanes:

| Organ | Mode | Cadence | Primary Constraint |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **I** | Theory / Meaning | Slow, irregular | No audience optimization; obscurity permitted |
| **II** | Art / Experience | Project-based | Presence required; explanation not |
| **III** | Commerce / Labor | Deadline-driven | Survives without defining values |
| **IV** | Orchestration | Steady/quiet | Coordination only; no content generation |
| **V** | Public Process | Sparse/rhythmic | Legibility without resolution |
| **VI** | Community | Human | Quality over scale; commitment-gated |
| **VII** | Marketing | Consistent/detached | Mechanical routing; no sincerity |

The architecture prevents three pathologies:

*   **Art being corrupted by commerce** (III interfaces to public via IV, not directly)
*   **Theory being compromised by scale** (I explicitly prohibited from audience optimization)
*   **Community being colonized by attention metrics** (VI receives only filtered entries, post-commitment)

* * *

### 2. **Key Design Tensions & Assumptions**

**Assumption 1: Separation requires active orchestration.** You cannot simply wall off these functions passively. Organ IV exists because without deliberate mediation, higher-velocity organs (Marketing, Commerce) naturally colonize lower-velocity ones (Theory, Art). This is structurally sound but operationally demanding—orchestration is invisible labor.

**Assumption 2: Incompleteness and contradiction are structural, not failures.** Theory (I) is explicitly permitted to "remain unused for long periods," contradict itself, and stay obscure. This is protective against premature resolution. But it assumes you have institutional patience and economic coverage (Organ III) to afford this.

**Assumption 3: Scale is the enemy of integrity.** Community (VI) is explicitly anti-growth. Marketing (VII) is purely mechanical. This assumes you prefer depth and continuity over reach. This is a value statement, not accidental.

* * *

### 3. **Structural Gaps & Vulnerabilities**

**Vulnerability 1: Orchestration single-point failure.** Organ IV holds all routing logic and boundary enforcement. If orchestration collapses, all other organs lose coherence. You have no redundancy or explicit escalation path if IV fails.

*   _Mitigation question:_ Who/what prevents orchestration from becoming bottleneck or corrupted?

**Vulnerability 2: Public Process (V) is a permeable membrane.** You describe V as the "membrane between system and world." It's designed to be unfinished and exploratory—but unfinished process can leak unresolved pressure directly to community or market. Boundaries blur easily here.

*   _Mitigation question:_ What prevents V from becoming a pressure valve that normalizes incompleteness as marketable rawness?

**Vulnerability 3: Sub-system 3 (Personal Maintenance) is infrastructure but not systematized.** You explicitly reject documenting it. But if it collapses silently, the diagnosis will be wrong (you'll blame the system design, not the load-bearing foundation).

*   _Mitigation question:_ How do you monitor infrastructure health without instrumentalizing it?

* * *

### 4. **Actionable Structural Decisions**

**Decision 1: Define Orchestration Explicitly** Right now, Organ IV's mechanisms are described as principles (say "not yet," maintain boundaries). You need operational specifics:

*   What does the "dependency logic" actually document? (e.g., decision tree, issue tracking, workflow state?)
*   How is routing decided? (e.g., review checkpoints, explicit graduation criteria?)
*   Who enforces it? (e.g., you alone, a trusted collaborator, async protocol?)

**Decision 2: Formalize Public Process Release Criteria** Organ V is the most permeable. Consider explicit gates:

*   What triggers something moving from Personal Profile → V?
*   What prevents V from becoming a default dump for unfinished work?
*   Is there a review layer before V-to-Community or V-to-Market routing?

**Decision 3: Establish Backplane Cadence** The three sub-systems (Admin, Archival, Personal) have no stated review cycle. Without periodic inspection, they decay silently:

*   Admin/Legal: quarterly or event-driven?
*   Archival: continuous (during production) or batch?
*   Personal: weekly rhythm check or reactive only?

* * *

### 5. **Diagnostic: Is This System Complete or Aspirational?**

**Current state reading:** This is a **prescriptive charter** written as if already operational. The closing section ("The system is now complete enough to operate") positions it as lock-down, not blueprint.

**Key question for you:** Are these seven organs + three sub-systems already active, or are they architectural targets? If active, which ones exist as documented practice vs. documented intent?

This matters because the document's power comes from _enforcement_, not design. A perfectly described system that isn't enforced is just philosophy.

* * *

### 6. **Recommended Next Steps**

1.  **Audit current practice against charter.** For each organ, document:
    *   What you actually do (cadence, interfaces, outputs)
    *   Where it diverges from the charter
    *   Why (legitimate friction, or drift?)
2.  **Operationalize Orchestration.** Define the mechanisms for routing, gatekeeping, and graduation. This is the lynchpin.
3.  **Establish backplane review cycles.** Personal maintenance especially: create a non-public checkpoint (monthly/quarterly) that asks: "Is load-bearing infrastructure healthy?"
4.  **Test the boundaries.** The real test comes when temptation arises (e.g., direct community pressure for art to explain itself, or raw theory to become marketable). Does the system hold?

* * *

### **Bottom Line**

This is a mature operating system, not an aspirational framework. It's designed to resolve—not hide—the actual tensions in creative-academic-commercial practice. Its strength is that it names the pathologies explicitly and builds walls where needed. Its vulnerability is that it requires continuous enforcement.

The closing question ("Which existing boundary am I trying not to enforce?") is your diagnostic tool. Use it.

Done

Yes, but with important distinctions. The framework is **principle-based enough to scale down**, but you'll hit friction at each level. Let me map it:

* * *

## **Level 1: Institutional Framework** (what the charter describes)

**Status: Fully coherent.** This is the design space it was written for. The seven organs + backplanes operate as distinct governance zones with clear economic and temporal separation.

* * *

## **Level 2: Local Development Workspace**

**Status: Viable, but requires translation.**

The directory/project structure could mirror the seven organs:

```plain text
~/workspace/
├── ORGAN_I_theory/           # Conceptual work (unfinished, private-default)
│   ├── grammars/
│   ├── ontologies/
│   └── notebooks/
├── ORGAN_II_art/             # Experiential projects
│   ├── performance-xyz/
│   ├── installation-abc/
│   └── scores/
├── ORGAN_III_commerce/       # Client work, billable
│   ├── client-a/
│   ├── tools/
│   └── contracts/
├── ORGAN_IV_orchestration/   # Internal routing & decisions
│   ├── dependency-log/
│   ├── graduation-criteria/
│   └── archival-index/
├── ORGAN_V_public/           # Essays, notebooks, fragments
│   ├── essays/
│   ├── marginalia/
│   └── process-traces/
├── ORGAN_VI_community/       # Gated/private conversations
│   ├── salon-transcripts/
│   └── reading-group-notes/
├── ORGAN_VII_marketing/      # Templates, schedulers, automation
│   ├── announcement-templates/
│   ├── republish-schedule/
│   └── social-calendar/
└── BACKPLANE/
    ├── admin/                # Legal, contracts, accounting
    ├── archival/             # Versioning, memory index
    └── personal/             # (not tracked, but monitored)
```

**Advantages:**

*   File location enforces boundary thinking (you physically move things as they graduate)
*   Search/grep queries can be organ-scoped
*   Backup/privacy can be granular (III and VI get different treatment)
*   Documentation location matches organizational intent

**Friction points:**

*   **Cross-organ dependencies are spatial now, not just conceptual.** If theory (I) feeds into art (II), you need symlink discipline or explicit import conventions. This becomes tedious at scale.
*   **Orchestration becomes a folder, not a process.** Organ IV's core job is _deciding_ what moves. A folder doesn't decide; it just holds the decision log. You still need the person/process that manages it.
*   **Git history and file history diverge.** A piece of work graduates from I→V→VI. Does it stay in ORGAN_I and get copied? Or move? Both approaches break something.

* * *

## **Level 3: GitHub Organization Structure**

**Status: Works, but needs careful naming and permission design.**

```plain text
GitHub Organization: [your-org]
├── organ-i-theory              # Private or internal
│   ├── grammar-systems
│   ├── ontology-sketches
│   └── research-notebooks
├── organ-ii-art                # Mixed public/private
│   ├── performance-2025
│   ├── installation-protocols
│   └── [private] scores-wip
├── organ-iii-commerce          # Private
│   ├── [private] client-a-site
│   ├── [private] tools-consulting
│   └── services-catalog
├── organ-iv-orchestration      # Private or internal
│   ├── [public-access-read-only] dependency-log
│   ├── graduation-standards
│   └── archival-index
├── organ-v-public              # Fully public
│   ├── essays-and-notes
│   ├── marginalia
│   └── process-documentation
├── organ-vi-community          # Private, team-access
│   ├── [invitation-only] salon-archive
│   └── reading-group-notes
├── organ-vii-marketing         # Private or internal
│   ├── announcement-templates
│   ├── social-automation
│   └── scheduling-tools
└── backplane                   # Private
    ├── [private] admin-legal
    ├── [private] archival-index
    └── [private] maintenance-notes
```

**Advantages:**

*   **Permission model enforces boundaries.** Organ III is private. Organ V is public. Organ VI is gated-access. This is GitHub's native language.
*   **Visibility is default-correct.** You don't have to remember which folder is which; the GitHub UI shows you exactly who can see what.
*   **Collaboration is scoped.** You can invite people to Organ VI (community) without granting access to Organ III (commerce).
*   **Issue/PR workflows can enforce routing.** You might enforce a rule: "PRs in Organ I require full prose review. PRs in Organ III require client sign-off."

**Friction points:**

*   **Orchestration becomes a meta-repo, not a process.** Organ IV's core function is _deciding_. A repository can _document_ decisions, but it can't make them. You still need the async/sync mechanism that routes things.
*   **Graduated work gets messy.** When something moves from Organ I→V→VI, does it:
    *   Live in multiple repos (duplication)?
    *   Exist as references/links (fragmentation)?
    *   Get archived in one and active in another (confusion)?You need a documented "promotion protocol."
*   **Private repos create visibility debt.** Organ IV (orchestration) and Organ I (theory) will likely be private. But the more private repos you have, the less transparent the system becomes from outside. You'll need an archival strategy that surfaces summaries into public space.

* * *

## **The Integration Problem**

The three levels are **not isomorphic**. Here's where they conflict:

| Dimension | Local FS | GitHub |
| --- | --- | --- |
| **Granularity** | Files/folders | Repos (coarser) |
| **Permissions** | Filesystem ownership | Organization roles |
| **History** | File history | Commit history + PR history |
| **Routing** | You copy/move files | You decide: fork, branch, or reference |
| **Discoverability** | Directory traversal | GitHub search + org structure |

**Example tension:** Organ V (public process) might contain 50 markdown notes. In local FS, these live in `ORGAN_V_public/essays/`. On GitHub, do they all live in one `organ-v-public` repo, or do they scatter across multiple repos based on topic?

If **one repo**, the repo becomes a catch-all and loses semantic coherence. If **multiple repos**, you lose the visual coherence of "the public process organ."

* * *

## **Recommendation: Hybrid Structure**

**Use GitHub as the primary source of truth for boundaries.** Locally, use the folder structure as a **working cache**, not the authoritative layer.

Here's the workflow:

1.  **Local workspace mirrors the seven organs** (helps you think structurally)
2.  **GitHub repos align with _output categories_, not organs**
    *   `organ-v-public` (essays, marginalia, all public process in one place)
    *   `organ-ii-art-performances` (all performances, across multiple organ interactions)
    *   `tools-and-services` (client work, open-source tools, services)
    *   `theory-archives` (publications, formalized outputs from Organ I)
    *   `community-and-conversation` (gated, invitation-only)
    *   `backplane-admin` (private, operational)
3.  **Orchestration becomes a protocol document** (in `organ-iv-orchestration` repo or in backplane):
    *   Decision log (what graduated, when, why?)
    *   Promotion criteria (when does something move from I→V?)
    *   Archive index (where did old work go?)
    *   Permission matrix (who can see what?)
4.  **Archival layer links them together:**
    *   Maintain an index that maps local working folders → GitHub repos → published/archived state
    *   Use consistent tagging across repos (v1, v2, archived, experimental, production)
    *   Regular sync: pull from GitHub, work locally, push back

* * *

## **Bottom Line**

| Question | Answer |
| --- | --- |
| Does it make sense as institutional framework? | **Yes, completely.** This is its native design space. |
| As a local development workspace? | **Yes, with discipline.** Requires naming conventions and move/copy protocols. |
| As a GitHub org structure? | **Yes, but permission-mapped, not organ-mapped.** Repos are outputs/roles, not organs. |
| All three simultaneously? | **Yes, if you treat each as a different abstraction level.** Local FS = working layer. GitHub = publishing/collaboration layer. Institutional = decision/governance layer. |

The **key insight:** Organs are _governance units_, not _file containers_. They define cadence, permissions, and interfaces. The _container_ (folder, repo, database) is secondary—it just makes the governance visible and enforceable.

1.  Connects the three layers (local FS, GitHub, institutional governance)

## **Promotion/Graduation Protocol**

A work progresses through state transitions. The protocol defines when, how, and under what conditions.

* * *

## **1. State Model**

Every piece of work exists in one of these states:

```plain text
LOCAL (private, unresolved)
    ↓
CANDIDATE (ready to be evaluated for promotion)
    ↓
[ORCHESTRATION GATE]
    ↓
PUBLIC_PROCESS (V) — visible but unresolved
    ↓
[ORCHESTRATION GATE]
    ↓
GRADUATED (II, III, or VI depending on type)
    ↓
ARCHIVED (preserved, reference-only)
```

**Key:** Not all work moves through all states. Some lives in LOCAL forever. Some jumps from LOCAL directly to III (commerce). Theory might cycle LOCAL→CANDIDATE→LOCAL indefinitely.

* * *

## **2. State Definitions with Operational Criteria**

### **LOCAL** (Private, unresolved)

**Location:** `~/workspace/ORGAN_*_*/` (local only, not in GitHub) **Duration:** Indefinite **Permissions:** You only

**Criteria for this state:**

*   Work is mid-process, contradictory, or incomplete
*   No external audience yet
*   Ideas are fragile and not ready for routing logic
*   Experimentation is the default mode

**Examples:**

*   Draft essay with structural problems
*   Half-finished generative art prototype
*   Research notes that contradict each other
*   Client proposal still being negotiated

* * *

### **CANDIDATE** (Ready for evaluation, still private)

**Location:** `~/workspace/ORGAN_*_*/` + tagged branch in GitHub **Duration:** 2 weeks – 3 months (review window) **Permissions:** You + designated reviewer(s) if applicable

**Criteria for promotion to CANDIDATE:**

*   The work has stabilized enough to describe its own trajectory
*   You can articulate: "This wants to become [art / theory / public process / tool]"
*   If collaborative, all authors have signed off on direction
*   A decision is needed: what happens next?

**Operational trigger:** You create a **promotion proposal** (see section 4 for format).

**What happens in CANDIDATE state:**

*   Work lives in a `branch/organ-*-candidate-[work-id]` on GitHub
*   README at branch root explicitly states: "This is under review for promotion"
*   You (or orchestration delegate) review against graduation criteria
*   One of three outcomes:
    1.  **Promote** → moves to appropriate next state
    2.  **Return to LOCAL** → needs more work, branch archived
    3.  **Reject** → work doesn't fit system, becomes personal archive

* * *

### **PUBLIC_PROCESS** (Visible, unresolved — ORGAN V)

**Location:** `organ-v-public` repo on GitHub (public) **Duration:** 2 weeks – 2 years **Permissions:** Public read, you (author) + orchestration write

**Criteria for promotion to PUBLIC_PROCESS:**

*   Work is legible enough for others to see without explanation
*   You're comfortable with rough edges being visible
*   The work benefits from being _seen_ (even incompletely)
*   It does NOT need to be fully resolved

**What this state is for:**

*   Essays with unresolved conclusions
*   Research notes and annotations
*   Process traces, rehearsal documentation
*   Fragments and partial thoughts
*   Methodology sketches

**What this state is NOT:**

*   Finished products
*   Polished marketing copy
*   Daily life logging
*   Performance-optimized content

**Operational requirements:**

*   **Metadata file** (see section 4): explains what this is, why it's public, what resolution is needed
*   **Archive pointer**: if this later graduates or changes, the public_process version remains frozen
*   **Backlink**: in `organ-iv-orchestration/archival-index`, register this work with its state

* * *

### **GRADUATED** (Active, assigned to an organ — II, III, or VI)

**Location:** Organ-specific repos on GitHub **Duration:** Project-active (months to years) **Permissions:** Depends on organ (II: mixed, III: private, VI: gated)

**Criteria for promotion to GRADUATED:**

**If moving to ORGAN II (Art/Experience):**

*   Presence is achieved (performed, exhibited, released, or documented)
*   The work has temporal or experiential coherence
*   It does not require explanation to exist
*   You're comfortable with it being judged on its own terms

**If moving to ORGAN III (Commerce):**

*   Contract is signed or scope is locked
*   Deliverables are specified
*   Timeline is committed
*   Money has changed hands or is imminent

**If moving to ORGAN VI (Community):**

*   Work has stabilized into a format that invites participation
*   You're ready to discuss it with committed people
*   It can survive critique without collapsing
*   Access is by invitation or explicit gating

* * *

### **ARCHIVED** (Reference only, no longer active)

**Location:** `backplane/archival-index/` with frozen copies **Duration:** Indefinite (preserved) **Permissions:** Read-only, reference

**Criteria for archival:**

*   The work has completed its active lifecycle
*   You want to preserve it for:
    *   Historical reference
    *   Future scholarship
    *   Teaching material
    *   Portfolio documentation
*   It will not be maintained or updated

**Operational mechanics:**

*   Work is **frozen** at a specific commit/version
*   Moved to archival branch or separate repo (e.g., `archive/2024-projects`)
*   Entry created in archival index (see section 4)
*   Original repo may be deleted, archived on GitHub, or marked read-only

* * *

## **3. Decision Matrix: Which State → Which State?**

Not all transitions are allowed. This matrix shows valid paths:

```plain text
FROM LOCAL:
  → CANDIDATE (always allowed)
  → [SKIP to PUBLIC_PROCESS] (only if you are confident in direction)
  → [SKIP to GRADUATED] (only if organ is clear & conditions met)
  → Stays LOCAL (indefinitely allowed)

FROM CANDIDATE:
  → PUBLIC_PROCESS (if ready to be visible but unfinished)
  → GRADUATED (if ready for full commitment)
  → LOCAL (rejected or needs more work)
  → ARCHIVED (consciously abandoned)

FROM PUBLIC_PROCESS:
  → GRADUATED (if completed or committed to organ)
  → ARCHIVED (if time-bounded or concluded)
  → LOCAL (if needs major revision; rare)
  → [NO RETURN] Can only move forward or archive

FROM GRADUATED:
  → ARCHIVED (when active work concludes)
  → [STAYS GRADUATED] Can remain active indefinitely
  → [NO SIDEWAYS] Cannot move to a different organ once graduated

FROM ARCHIVED:
  → [STAYS ARCHIVED] (immutable)
```

**Key rule:** Work can move forward or sideways into a compatible organ. It cannot move backward except from CANDIDATE.

* * *

## **4. Operational Artifacts**

Each promotion requires documentation. Here's what gets created:

### **4a. Promotion Proposal** (CANDIDATE state trigger)

**File:** `organ-iv-orchestration/proposals/[work-id]-[date]-proposal.md`

**Format:**

markdown
```markdown
# Promotion Proposal: [Work Title]

## Work ID
`[organ]-[work-type]-[timestamp]`
(e.g., `organ-i-theory-grammar-2025-01-15`)

## Current State
LOCAL

## Proposed State
CANDIDATE → [target state: PUBLIC_PROCESS / GRADUATED / ARCHIVED]

## Summary
[2-3 sentences on what this work is and why it matters]

## Trajectory
Where do you think this wants to become?
(art / theory / tool / publication / nothing yet)

## Completion Status
- [ ] Structurally stable
- [ ] All collaborators aligned
- [ ] No critical blockers
- [ ] Ready for external eyes (if moving to PUBLIC_PROCESS or GRADUATED)

## Decision Needed
What question does orchestration need to answer?
(e.g., "Should this be public or gated?" / "Is this client-ready?")

## References
- Local path: `~/workspace/ORGAN_X_*/[path]`
- GitHub branch (if exists): `branch/organ-*-candidate-[work-id]`
- Related work: [links to upstream theory, collaborators, etc.]

## Proposer
[You / collaborator]

## Date Proposed
[YYYY-MM-DD]
```

### **4b. Graduation Criteria Checklist** (CANDIDATE → GRADUATED)

**File:** `organ-iv-orchestration/graduation-criteria-[organ].md`

**Example for ORGAN II (Art):**

markdown
```markdown
# Graduation Criteria: ORGAN II (Art / Experience)

## Minimum Requirements
- [ ] Work has been experienced (performed, exhibited, or documented)
- [ ] Documentation exists (photos, video, notes, scores)
- [ ] Title and date are finalized
- [ ] It does not require author explanation to exist
- [ ] You are comfortable with public judgment

## Metadata Required
- [ ] Title, date, medium/format
- [ ] 1-2 sentence description (not explanation)
- [ ] Collaborators named
- [ ] Documentation license (CC, copyright, or restricted)

## GitHub Setup
- [ ] Repo created: `organ-ii-art-[project-slug]`
- [ ] README exists with minimum metadata
- [ ] All assets committed
- [ ] Issues/PRs closed or migrated

## Archival Registration
- [ ] Entry added to `archival-index/registry.json`
- [ ] Backed up to `backplane/archival/`
```

**Example for ORGAN III (Commerce):**

markdown
```markdown
# Graduation Criteria: ORGAN III (Commerce)

## Minimum Requirements
- [ ] Signed contract (or written scope + authorization)
- [ ] Deliverables specified
- [ ] Timeline agreed
- [ ] Payment terms documented
- [ ] Client access level decided

## GitHub Setup
- [ ] Private repo created: `organ-iii-commerce-[client-slug]`
- [ ] Access restricted to relevant team members + client
- [ ] README with scope summary (internal use)
- [ ] Invoice/payment tracking linked

## Financial Registration
- [ ] Entry in accounting system (ORGAN backplane/admin)
- [ ] Milestone schedule documented
- [ ] IP ownership clarified
```

### **4c. Metadata File** (All states)

**File:** `[repo-root]/.organ-metadata.json`

**Format:**

json
```json
{
  "work_id": "organ-v-public-essay-temporal-systems-2025-01",
  "title": "On Temporal Systems in Digital Art",
  "organ": "V",
  "state": "PUBLIC_PROCESS",
  "created": "2024-11-15",
  "last_updated": "2025-01-15",
  "author": ["you@example.com"],
  "collaborators": [],
  "upstream_theory": [
    "organ-i-theory-temporality-sketch-2024",
    "publication-2023-archive"
  ],
  "description": "Unresolved notes on how digital systems create temporal experience.",
  "maturity": "exploratory",
  "resolution_needed": [
    "Formal conclusion to the temporal mechanics section",
    "Integration with practice examples"
  ],
  "next_state": null,
  "archival_plan": "Will move to GRADUATED (II) if it becomes a performance framework",
  "permissions": {
    "read": "public",
    "write": "author_only",
    "discuss": "issue_comments_enabled"
  },
  "license": "CC-BY-NC-SA-4.0",
  "tags": ["theory", "temporality", "digital-art", "unresolved"]
}
```

### **4d. Archival Index Entry** (All graduated + archived work)

**File:** `organ-iv-orchestration/archival-index/registry.md`

**Format:**

markdown
```markdown
## Work Registry

#### 2024-12

| Work ID | Title | Date | State | Duration | Repo | Archive Link | Notes |
|---------|-------|------|-------|----------|------|--------------|-------|

### ORGAN I: Theory

| Work ID | Title | State | Pub Status | Archive |
|---------|-------|-------|-----------|---------|
| org-i-theory-temporal-2024 | Temporal Systems Sketch | PUBLIC_PROCESS | [essay](link) | — |
| org-i-onto-symbols-2023 | Ontology of Symbols v2 | ARCHIVED | [pdf](link) | [frozen](link) |

### ORGAN III: Commerce

[Private registry, stored in backplane/admin]

### ORGAN VI: Community

[Gated registry, only visible to community members]
```

---

## **5. Git Workflow Integration**

The protocol lives in Git. Here's the branching strategy:
```
main (published, stable)
├── branch/organ-i-candidate-*         (Theory candidate)
├── branch/organ-ii-candidate-*        (Art candidate)
├── branch/organ-iii-commerce-[client] (Private, client work)
├── branch/organ-v-[essay-id]          (Public process, published)
├── branch/organ-vi-*                  (Community, gated)
└── archive/[year]/                    (Frozen old work)
```

### **Workflow for promoting LOCAL → CANDIDATE:**

bash
```bash
# 1. In local workspace, work on the piece
~/workspace/ORGAN_I_theory/grammar-systems/
  # Edit, commit locally (not pushed)

# 2. When ready, create promotion proposal
# File: ~/workspace/ORGAN_IV_orchestration/proposals/
# (This stays local for now)

# 3. Create GitHub branch for candidate review
git checkout -b branch/organ-i-candidate-grammar-systems-2025-01

# 4. Push candidate branch (not to main)
git push origin branch/organ-i-candidate-grammar-systems-2025-01

# 5. Create GitHub issue/discussion linking to proposal
# Title: "Promote: grammar-systems → [target state]"
# Body: links to proposal file

# 6. Orchestration reviews:
#    - Read proposal
#    - Check metadata
#    - Approve or request changes

# 7a. If approved → merge to main (or to organ-specific branch)
# 7b. If rejected → delete candidate branch, document in proposal
```

### **Workflow for promoting CANDIDATE → PUBLIC_PROCESS (ORGAN V):**

bash
```bash
# 1. Orchestration approves in GitHub issue

# 2. Create `.organ-metadata.json` in work root
# (state: PUBLIC_PROCESS)

# 3. Ensure all assets are in `organ-v-public` repo

# 4. Merge to main branch (public by default)

# 5. Update archival index:
organ-iv-orchestration/archival-index/registry.md
  - Add entry with repo link, state, date

# 6. Delete candidate branch (work is now public)

# 7. Tag the commit
git tag -a "org-v-public-[work-id]-promoted" -m "Promoted to ORGAN V"
git push origin --tags
```

### **Workflow for promoting CANDIDATE → GRADUATED (ORGAN II/III/VI):**

bash
```bash
# 1. Orchestration approves + checks graduation criteria

# 2. If ORGAN III (commerce): keep on private branch
#    If ORGAN II (art): merge to main or organ-specific repo
#    If ORGAN VI (community): move to private repo with gated access

# 3. Update metadata: state = GRADUATED

# 4. Register in archival index with active project link

# 5. If moving from PUBLIC_PROCESS → GRADUATED:
#    - Keep public version frozen (tag it)
#    - Active version goes to graduated organ repo
#    - Archival index notes both versions

# 6. Set up issue/project board for active work (if needed)
```

### **Workflow for GRADUATED → ARCHIVED:**

bash
```bash
# 1. When project is complete:
#    - Freeze current state (tag commit)
#    - Mark repo as read-only (GitHub settings) or move to archive org

# 2. Create archival entry:
git checkout -b archive/[year]/[work-id]
# Commit freeze point + documentation
git push origin archive/[year]/[work-id]

# 3. Update registry:
organ-iv-orchestration/archival-index/registry.md
  - Change state to ARCHIVED
  - Link to archive commit/tag
  - Add closure notes

# 4. Optional: remove from active project list
#    (but keep in main history)
```

---

## **6. Orchestration Decision Protocol**

Organ IV doesn't just rubber-stamp. It actively gates. Here's the decision framework:

### **Questions Orchestration Asks at Each Promotion:**

**LOCAL → CANDIDATE:**
- Is this real work (not distraction)?
- Is it stable enough to evaluate?
- *Usually: auto-approved if criteria met*

**CANDIDATE → PUBLIC_PROCESS:**
- Does this benefit from being seen unfinished?
- Is it legible without author explanation?
- Does public visibility solve any pressure?
- Will it create confusion or attract wrong attention?

**CANDIDATE → GRADUATED (ORGAN II):**
- Has presence been achieved?
- Is the work ready to stand on its own?
- Does it fit with other active art projects?
- Will active maintenance be required?

**CANDIDATE → GRADUATED (ORGAN III):**
- Is the contract clear?
- Does the client relationship have defined boundaries?
- Does billing infrastructure exist?
- Will this distract from other work?

**CANDIDATE → GRADUATED (ORGAN VI):**
- Is the work coherent enough for critique?
- Are you ready for this community to engage deeply?
- Will this strengthen or dilute community coherence?

**ANY → ARCHIVED:**
- Is the active lifecycle actually complete?
- Is preservation handled (backups, metadata)?
- Could this become active again? (If yes, consider dormant instead of archived)
- Is closure documented?

---

## **7. State Monitoring & Enforcement**

The system decays without monitoring. Set cadence:

### **Weekly** (you, 15 min)
- Review LOCAL work for anything stuck in LOCAL too long
- Ask: "Should any LOCAL become CANDIDATE?"
- Flag anything that's creating pressure without advancing

### **Biweekly** (you, 30 min)
- Check all CANDIDATE work
- Ask: "Is this still being evaluated, or is it stalled?"
- CANDIDATE shouldn't live >3 months without decision

### **Monthly** (you + designated reviewer if applicable, 1 hr)
- Review all GRADUATED work
- Ask: "Is anything ready to ARCHIVE?"
- Ensure archival index is current
- Check that backups are happening

### **Quarterly** (you, 2 hrs)
- Audit the entire system
- Walk through all repos and compare to registry
- Check that metadata files are consistent
- Review orchestration log for patterns
  - Are certain organs under/over-loaded?
  - Is anything stuck in a state too long?
  - Are boundaries being honored?

### **Annually** (you + outside perspective if possible, half day)
- Review the protocol itself
- Did it work? Where did it fail?
- Update graduation criteria if needed
- Archive full year's work properly
- Reset year's workflow

---

## **8. Example: A Work Moving Through the System**

**January 15: Generative art idea born in LOCAL**
```
~/workspace/ORGAN_II_art/generative-study-2025/
- code sketches
- parameter explorations
- no documentation yet
```

**February 1: Stabilizes, moved to CANDIDATE**
```
branch/organ-ii-candidate-generative-study-2025-01

Proposal created:
- "This wants to become a performance piece"
- "Need feedback on visual direction"
- "Will collaborate with musician if approved"

Orchestration question: "Is collaborative structure clear?"
```

**February 15: Approved, moved to PUBLIC_PROCESS**
```
organ-v-public repo
- Published early code + visuals
- Unresolved: "How does sound interact?"
- Community can see development

Metadata notes: "Unfinished, seeking feedback"
```

**April 1: Direction clarified, collaborative partner confirmed**
```
CANDIDATE again (briefly)

New proposal: "Move to GRADUATED ORGAN II"
Graduation criteria:
- [ ] Collaboration terms documented ✓
- [ ] Code infrastructure stable ✓
- [ ] Visual identity finalized ✓
- [ ] Performance timeline planned ✓
```

**April 15: GRADUATED to ORGAN II**
```
organ-ii-art-generative-performance-2025 repo
- Private (development)
- Collaboration tracked in issues
- Code, documentation, performance notes
- Performance scheduled: June 2025
```

**July 1: Performance complete**
```
Graduating from GRADUATED → ARCHIVED

archive/2025/org-ii-generative-performance-2025/
- Frozen commit of final code
- Performance documentation
- Recording + notes
- Archival entry created

Public version (from ORGAN V):
- Frozen at time of performance
- Links to performance documentation
- Marked read-only

Result: Work exists in two frozen states
- Public process (early exploration)
- Archive (completed work + performance traces)
```

* * *

## **9. Backplane Integration**

The three sub-systems (Admin, Archival, Personal) support the protocol:

### **Admin (Legal/Financial)**

*   Every GRADUATED III work: contract file in backplane/admin
*   Every GRADUATED work: licensing/IP clarification documented
*   Annual review of all active commercial work

### **Archival (Memory)**

*   Registry is single source of truth
*   Every archived work: frozen commit + metadata preserved
*   Search index updated quarterly (what exists, where, when)

### **Personal Maintenance**

*   Weekly LOCAL review: Are you using LOCAL as dumping ground or thinking space?
*   Monthly GRADUATED check: Is active project load sustainable?
*   Quarterly audit: Is the system supporting you, or becoming overhead?

* * *

## **10. Enforcement: What Happens When Boundaries Break**

**If work bypasses orchestration** (e.g., you push directly from LOCAL to PUBLIC_PROCESS):

*   Monthly audit catches it
*   Rewind: retag the commit, follow protocol retroactively
*   Reflect: Why did you bypass? (Often signals protocol isn't serving you)

**If CANDIDATE gets stuck >3 months:**

*   Orchestration asks: Return to LOCAL, reject, or force decision?
*   Document the delay in proposal file
*   Update protocol if needed

**If GRADUATED work is abandoned:**

*   Move to ARCHIVED, not left hanging
*   Document: "Paused indefinitely" or "Concluded"

**If you feel tempted to add another organ:**

*   Trigger the diagnostic question: "Which boundary am I trying not to enforce?"
*   Likely answer: orchestration isn't working well enough, or personal maintenance is failing
*   Fix the infrastructure, not the architecture

* * *

## **Bottom Line**

This protocol makes the invisible (decisions about what's ready, what's public, what's private) **explicit and traceable**.

The real power isn't the states—it's the **decision log**. A year from now, you'll know exactly when work moved from theory to art to archive, why, and what changed. That's reproducibility at the system level.

The protocol only works if you enforce it. Start with weekly audits. Add monthly orchestration reviews. The quarterly system audit will tell you if it's lightening your cognitive load or becoming busywork.

Does this level of operational detail match how you actually work, or does it need adjustment?

2.  **On being overkill**: Possibly. Here's the thing:
    *   Do they need Zenodo DOI integration right now? Probably not day 1.
    *   Do they need git-cliff + Buttondown + semantic-release all configured simultaneously? That's a lot of moving parts.
    *   Does the central registry need to be that sophisticated initially? Could start much simpler.
    *   The metadata frontmatter standard with all those fields—useful, but can start minimal.
    *   Cross-repo dispatch workflows—useful for multi-organ work, but can be added incrementally.
3.  **On overthinking**: I think they're asking: "Am I designing a system to work, or designing a system to design the system?"

The honest answer: The design IS elegant and logical. But the _implementation_ could be phased. The problem with what I wrote is it presents the _complete_ architecture as if it needs to exist on Day 1. That's a mental burden, even if technically lazy afterward.

A better approach: start minimal with just repo naming conventions, a basic central registry, GitHub Pages for the public site, and a handful of core workflows (release to public, release to social). Metadata can be optional YAML frontmatter rather than mandatory everywhere. Then layer in sophistication—DOI integration, semantic versioning, cross-repo orchestration—as actual friction points emerge rather than preemptively.

There's also a subtle distinction I'm noticing: "maximum automation" could mean either investing 40 hours upfront to design a system that then runs free, or starting lean and automating incrementally. Given their preference for high-level work and their stated laziness, the second path probably serves them better.

The architecture itself is sound and not overthought. The real issue is trying to implement everything simultaneously. A phased rollout—MVP in week one, then expanding over weeks two through four—would deliver most of the value without the initial setup burden.

Done

**Overkill?** Probably _if implemented all at once on Day 1_.

You don't need Zenodo DOIs, git-cliff changelogs, n8n Patreon integration, and semantic-release configured simultaneously to start working. That's architecture theater.

## How They Connect

```
registry.json (data)
    ↓ [tells automation what repos exist and their relationships]
    ↓
orchestration-system.md (rules)
    ↓ [tells automation when repos can transition between organs]
    ↓
github-actions-spec.md (workflows)
    ↓ [implements these rules as automated GitHub Actions]
    ↓ [triggers publish-process which calls...]
    ↓
public-process-map.md (output)
    ↓ [essays published, then distributed via...]
    ↓
ORGAN-VII (Marketing) — future document
    ↓ [amplifies to audience]
```

**Data flow:**
- Registry is the schema (what exists)
- Governance is the logic (what transitions are valid)
- Workflows are the executors (how transitions happen automatically)
- Public Process is the output (what gets shared publicly)

```markdown
# ORGAN-IV: Orchestration System

**Status:** Design Document (Ready to Implement)  
**Version:** 1.0  
**Created:** 2026-02-03  
**Owner:** ORGAN-IV (to be established)

---

## Executive Summary

The Orchestration System governs workflow across all seven organs. It defines:
1. **Promotion criteria** — What qualifies a repo to graduate from one organ to another
2. **Dependency rules** — Cross-organ dependency tracking and validation
3. **Routing logic** — How work flows between organs
4. **Health checks** — Automated validation of system coherence

This document is the data layer for ORGAN-IV automation. Once implemented, all GitHub Actions workflows reference these rules.

---

## Table of Contents

1. [Core Concepts](#core-concepts)
2. [Promotion Criteria](#promotion-criteria)
3. [Dependency Rules](#dependency-rules)
4. [Routing Logic](#routing-logic)
5. [Health Checks & Monitoring](#health-checks--monitoring)
6. [Implementation Architecture](#implementation-architecture)

---

## Core Concepts

### Repo Lifecycle States

Every repo exists in one of these states:

```
IDEATION → SCAFFOLDING → ACTIVE → MATURE → ARCHIVED
```

**IDEATION**  
- Hypothesis stage, minimal code  
- Belongs to: ORGAN-I (Theory)  
- Requirements: README with problem statement  
- Can promote to: SCAFFOLDING (upon initial architecture design)  

**SCAFFOLDING**  
- Framework exists, examples incomplete  
- Belongs to: ORGAN-II (Art), or ORGAN-I (Theory)  
- Requirements: API documented, at least 1 working example  
- Can promote to: ACTIVE (upon working implementation with tests)  

**ACTIVE**  
- In production or regular use  
- Belongs to: ORGAN-II (Art), ORGAN-III (Commerce), ORGAN-V (Public Process)  
- Requirements: Tests pass, docs current, 30+ days updated  
- Can promote to: MATURE (upon 1+ year stability, significant usage)  

**MATURE**  
- Proven, stable, widely adopted  
- Belongs to: ORGAN-III (Commerce), ORGAN-V (Public Process)  
- Requirements: SLA-level reliability, comprehensive docs, community adoption  
- Can promote to: ARCHIVED (when sunset planned)  

**ARCHIVED**  
- End-of-life, read-only  
- Requirements: Migration path documented  
- Never promotes; can only be deleted after 6-month read-only period

### Organ Classification

Repos **primarily belong to one organ**, but can **cross-participate** in others (modeled in registry as multi-organ relationships).

**Primary organ assignment criteria:**

| Organ | Primary Type | Graduation Condition |
|-------|---|---|
| ORGAN-I (Theory) | Epistemological framework | Generalized beyond single implementation |
| ORGAN-II (Art) | Artistic system, experience, performance | Demonstrated in exhibition/performance context |
| ORGAN-III (Commerce) | Revenue product, B2B/B2C/B2B2C | Live paying customers or measurable revenue |
| ORGAN-IV (Orchestration) | Cross-organ tooling, governance, automation | Proven effective across 2+ other organs |
| ORGAN-V (Public Process) | Essays, marginalia, changelog, process docs | Published and receiving audience engagement |
| ORGAN-VI (Community) | Community infrastructure, membership, shared resources | 3+ active community members using it regularly |
| ORGAN-VII (Marketing) | Content distribution, POSSE, audience amplification | Measurable audience growth or engagement metrics |

---

## Promotion Criteria

### Theory → Art Promotion

**Condition:** A Theory framework is implemented as a concrete Art system.

**Criteria (all required):**
- [ ] Framework has been used to generate at least 1 working artwork
- [ ] Artwork demonstrates novel aesthetic or interaction model
- [ ] Code is published with example project
- [ ] GitHub repo tagged with both `ORGAN-I` and `ORGAN-II` topics
- [ ] PR opened linking theory repo to art repo (relationship documented in registry)

**Outcome:** Theory repo gains "implemented-in" cross-reference; Art repo gains "implements" cross-reference.

**Example:**
- `auto-revision-epistemic-engine` (ORGAN-I) → implemented in generative music system (ORGAN-II)
- Registry updated with bidirectional link

---

### Art → Commerce Promotion

**Condition:** An Art system is packaged as a revenue product.

**Criteria (all required):**
- [ ] System has 3+ documented use cases or examples
- [ ] Pricing model defined (if B2B/B2C) or integration path (if embedded)
- [ ] API/integration documented with >500 words of docs
- [ ] At least 1 paying customer or active deployment
- [ ] GitHub repo has commerce topic added
- [ ] Governance doc created (contract, pricing, SLA, if applicable)
- [ ] README updated with commercial terms and support model

**Outcome:** Art repo gains "commercialized" status; Commerce repo gains "derived-from" cross-reference.

**Example:**
- `core-engine` (ORGAN-II) + `metasystem-master` (ORGAN-II) → `classroom-rpg-aetheria` (ORGAN-III)

---

### Theory → Commerce Promotion (Direct)

**Condition:** A Theory framework is directly commercialized without intermediate Art step.

**Criteria (all required):**
- [ ] Framework has clear B2B/B2C application  
- [ ] Minimum viable product exists (not just theory)
- [ ] All Theory promotion criteria met
- [ ] At least 1 paying customer or funded development
- [ ] Commercial terms documented in private governance repo

**Outcome:** Commerce repo tagged with both `ORGAN-I` and `ORGAN-III` topics; dual cross-reference recorded.

**Example:**
- `call-function--ontological` (ORGAN-I) → potential direct commercialization as API service

---

### Art/Theory → Public Process Promotion

**Condition:** Development process, methodology, or learnings are documented publicly.

**Criteria (all required):**
- [ ] Essay or process document written (minimum 2,000 words)
- [ ] Document linked to source code repo
- [ ] Published in ORGAN-V public process repo
- [ ] Includes methodology, decisions, and learnings
- [ ] Receives engagement (comments, shares, citations)

**Outcome:** Source repo gains "documented-in" cross-reference; ORGAN-V repo gains "documents" cross-reference.

**Example:**
- `narratological-algorithmic-lenses` → "How We Formalized Narrative as Algorithm" essay

---

### Public Process → Marketing Promotion

**Condition:** Public process document is amplified for audience reach.

**Criteria (all required):**
- [ ] Essay published in ORGAN-V with engagement metrics
- [ ] POSSE checklist completed (cross-posted to 3+ platforms)
- [ ] Newsletter included or standalone announcement sent
- [ ] Social media amplification documented
- [ ] Minimum 50 engaged readers or equivalent metrics

**Outcome:** Document gains "distributed" status; ORGAN-VII repo records amplification details.

---

### Multi-Organ Participation

**Rules:**

1. **A repo can belong to 2 organs maximum** (except ORGAN-IV which is overhead)
   - Example: `multi-camera--livestream--framework` = ORGAN-II + ORGAN-III

2. **Primary organ is the dominant use case**
   - `multi-camera--livestream--framework` is primarily ORGAN-III (commerce product), secondarily ORGAN-II (performance platform)

3. **Cross-participation documented in registry**
   - Relationship type: "cross_organ_participation"
   - Governance: Secondary organ inherits primary organ's promotion rules

4. **Decision rule: If unsure, assign to primary revenue/impact organ**
   - Theory always primary if theoretical contribution is novel
   - Commerce always primary if revenue-generating

---

## Dependency Rules

### Dependency Graph Validation

Every repo declares its dependencies. The system validates:

```
dependency_graph = {
  repo_name: {
    depends_on: [list of upstream repos/organs],
    consumed_by: [list of downstream repos/organs],
    transitive_depth: N,  # How many hops to reach ORGAN-I
    integrity_check: PASS/WARN/FAIL
  }
}
```

### Validation Rules

1. **No Circular Dependencies**
   - If A depends on B, B cannot depend on A
   - Exception: ORGAN-IV can depend on any repo (for orchestration)
   - Automated check: Monthly GitHub Actions workflow

2. **Upward Dependencies Only**
   - ORGAN-I (Theory) depends on nothing
   - ORGAN-II (Art) can depend on ORGAN-I or other ORGAN-II
   - ORGAN-III (Commerce) can depend on ORGAN-I, ORGAN-II, or other ORGAN-III
   - ORGAN-V/VI/VII depend on any organ (they're meta-organs)
   - Automated check: Every commit via pre-push hook

3. **Depth Limits**
   - Max transitive depth: 4 hops (to keep systems modular)
   - Warning at 3 hops; error at 4+
   - Exception: ORGAN-IV orchestration workflows can traverse entire graph

4. **Breaking Change Protocol**
   - If ORGAN-I repo makes breaking change:
     - All ORGAN-II repos must be updated within 30 days
     - All ORGAN-III repos must be updated within 60 days
   - GitHub issue opened in each dependent repo
   - Orchestration system tracks compliance

### Dependency Declaration Format

Each repo has a `.meta/dependencies.json` file:

```json
{
  "repo_name": "my-awesome-engine",
  "organ": "ORGAN-I",
  "status": "ACTIVE",
  "dependencies": {
    "internal": {
      "depends_on": [
        {
          "repo": "recursive-engine--generative-entity",
          "organ": "ORGAN-I",
          "type": "hard",
          "reason": "Core algorithm"
        }
      ],
      "consumed_by": [
        {
          "repo": "generative-art-system",
          "organ": "ORGAN-II",
          "type": "hard"
        }
      ]
    },
    "external": {
      "depends_on": [
        {
          "package": "numpy",
          "version": ">=1.21.0"
        }
      ]
    }
  }
}
```

---

## Routing Logic

### Work Routing Between Organs

#### Theory → Art Pipeline

```
ORGAN-I (Hypothesis)
    ↓ [meets implementation criteria]
ORGAN-II (Artistic Implementation)
    ↓ [meets commercialization criteria]
ORGAN-III (Commercial Product)
```

**Automated routing:**
1. Theory repo tagged with `ready-for-art` label
2. Orchestration system notifies ORGAN-II maintainers
3. Art repo created with prefix matching theory repo name
4. Cross-references established automatically
5. Dependency tracking updated

#### Commerce → Public Process Pipeline

```
ORGAN-III (Deployed Product)
    ↓ [meets documentation criteria]
ORGAN-V (Public Process Essay)
    ↓ [meets distribution criteria]
ORGAN-VII (Marketing Amplification)
```

**Automated routing:**
1. Commerce repo tagged with `publishable-process` label
2. Issue opened in ORGAN-V repo for essay assignment
3. After publication, essay tagged with `ready-to-distribute`
4. ORGAN-VII workflow triggers POSSE distribution
5. Engagement metrics tracked

#### Cross-Organ Contribution Flow

```
Community Member
    ↓ [proposes improvement]
Primary Organ Repo
    ↓ [if accepted and promoted]
Secondary Organ(s)
    ↓ [amplified in]
ORGAN-VII Marketing
```

**Automated routing:**
1. PR opened in any repo with `cross-organ-impact` label
2. Orchestration validates against all dependent repos
3. If approved, automatically pings secondary organs
4. On merge, dependency graph updated
5. Marketing queue updated if impact is significant

---

## Health Checks & Monitoring

### Monthly Organ Health Audit

**Automated via GitHub Actions:** `monthly-organ-audit.yml`

Checks per organ:

**ORGAN-I (Theory)**
- [ ] All repos have updated README with problem statement
- [ ] All repos have at least 1 example or test
- [ ] No circular dependencies detected
- [ ] Cross-organ references are current
- [ ] Promotion candidates identified (ready-for-art)

**ORGAN-II (Art)**
- [ ] All repos have working example (not SKELETON)
- [ ] All repos link to parent theory (if applicable)
- [ ] All repos have demo or visualization
- [ ] Portfolio repo populated with 3+ completed works
- [ ] Promotion candidates identified (ready-for-commerce)

**ORGAN-III (Commerce)**
- [ ] All repos have SLA documentation (public or private)
- [ ] All repos have update within 60 days
- [ ] Revenue tracking sheet current
- [ ] No undocumented private repos
- [ ] Customer agreement templates updated
- [ ] Candidates for ORGAN-V process documentation identified

**ORGAN-IV (Orchestration)**
- [ ] Central registry updated
- [ ] Governance rules documentation current
- [ ] All 46 repos mapped to organs
- [ ] Dependency graph valid (no circles, correct depth)
- [ ] All GitHub Actions workflows passing
- [ ] Automation runbooks current

**ORGAN-V (Public Process)**
- [ ] 2+ essays published in past 30 days
- [ ] Each essay linked to source repo
- [ ] Engagement metrics tracked
- [ ] Newsletter/RSS generated
- [ ] Candidates for ORGAN-VII amplification identified

**ORGAN-VI (Community)**
- [ ] Discord/forum active (if applicable)
- [ ] Community guidelines current
- [ ] Member count and engagement tracked
- [ ] Contribution workflows documented

**ORGAN-VII (Marketing)**
- [ ] 3+ POSSE campaigns completed in past 30 days
- [ ] Social metrics tracked
- [ ] Audience growth metrics analyzed
- [ ] Upcoming content calendar updated
- [ ] Newsletter subscriber count tracked

### Alert Conditions

**CRITICAL (immediate action required):**
- Circular dependency detected
- Private repo without governance doc
- ORGAN-III product without customer tracking
- Public repo with secrets exposed

**WARNING (address within 2 weeks):**
- Repo exceeds 60 days without update
- SKELETON repo with no examples
- ORGAN-V essay without linked source
- Marketing queue exceeds 3 weeks backlog

**INFO (review at monthly audit):**
- New repos awaiting organ assignment
- Completed promotions to record
- Cross-organ relationships to document

## Implementation Architecture

### Where ORGAN-IV Lives

**Recommended:** Create new org `4444J99-orchestration` with:

```
orchestration-start-here/
├── README.md (overview, getting started)
├── registry.json (this document's data structure)
├── governance-rules.json (Promotion criteria as code)
├── dependency-manifest.json (All 46 repos' dependencies)
├── .github/
│   └── workflows/
│       ├── monthly-organ-audit.yml
│       ├── validate-dependencies.yml
│       ├── promote-repo.yml
│       ├── publish-process.yml
│       └── distribute-content.yml
├── docs/
│   ├── promotion-process.md
│   ├── dependency-rules.md
│   ├── routing-logic.md
│   └── runbooks/
│       ├── how-to-promote-art-to-commerce.md
│       ├── how-to-publish-process.md
│       └── how-to-trigger-marketing-campaign.md
└── schemas/
    ├── repo-metadata.schema.json
    ├── dependency.schema.json
    └── promotion-criteria.schema.json
```

### Data Flow

```
Central Registry (registry.json)
    ↓ [read by all workflows]
GitHub Actions Workflows
    ↓ [validate against rules]
Governance Rules Engine (governance-rules.json)
    ↓ [determine routing]
Cross-Organ Dispatch System
    ↓ [push notifications/PRs]
Individual Organ Repos
    ↓ [update dependencies]
Monthly Audit (validate entire graph)
```

### Key Workflows (to be detailed in next document)

1. **validate-dependencies.yml** — Run on every PR across all repos; block merge if dependency rules violated
2. **monthly-organ-audit.yml** — Full system health check; generate report
3. **promote-repo.yml** — Triggered by label/comment; handles organ transitions
4. **publish-process.yml** — Triggered from ORGAN-III → automates ORGAN-V essay creation
5. **distribute-content.yml** — Triggered from ORGAN-V → POSSE/newsletter distribution

1. Create `orchestration-start-here` repo
2. Commit registry.json and this governance document
3. Create .github/workflows directory structure
4. Tag all existing repos with organ topics in GitHub

### Phase 2: Validation (Week 2)
1. Implement validate-dependencies.yml workflow
2. Test on all 46 repos (will find current violations)
3. Document any dependency conflicts found
4. Create runbooks for resolving violations

### Phase 3: Automation (Week 3-4)
1. Implement promotion, publishing, and distribution workflows
2. Test end-to-end: Theory → Art → Commerce → Process → Marketing
3. Run full monthly audit
4. Document and deploy

### Phase 4: Continuous Operation (Ongoing)
1. Monthly audit becomes scheduled task
2. New repos automatically onboarded to system
3. Promotion requests flow through automated pipeline
4. Cross-organ collaboration facilitated by clear routing

---

## Maintenance & Evolution

### Updating Governance Rules

**Process:**
1. Propose change as GitHub issue in orchestration repo
2. Comment period: 1 week
3. Vote among organ maintainers (simple majority)
4. Update governance-rules.json
5. Workflows automatically read new version on next run

### Handling Exceptions

**One-time exceptions** (e.g., "this theory repo will never be commercialized"):
1. Document in repo's `.meta/metadata.json`
2. Reference in orchestration audit log
3. Workflow honors exception via `ignore_rule: [list]`

**Systematic exceptions** (e.g., "private repos don't need cross-references"):
1. Propose new rule
2. Update governance document
3. Commit and merge

---

## Appendix: Example Governance Rules (JSON)

```json
{
  "version": "1.0",
  "rules": {
    "theory_to_art": {
      "name": "Theory can be implemented in Art",
      "conditions": [
        "depends_on: ORGAN-I repo",
        "has: working example or artwork",
        "has: public GitHub repo",
        "status: ACTIVE",
        "updated_within_days: 60"
      ],
      "action": "promote_to_art",
      "blockers": [
        "circular dependency detected",
        "dependent repos fail tests",
        "documentation outdated"
      ]
    },
    "art_to_commerce": {
      "name": "Art can be commercialized",
      "conditions": [
        "depends_on: ORGAN-I or ORGAN-II repos",
        "has: 3+ documented use cases",
        "has: API documentation (500+ words)",
        "has: paying customer OR active deployment",
        "status: ACTIVE",
        "updated_within_days: 30"
      ],
      "action": "promote_to_commerce",
      "blockers": [
        "circular dependency",
        "governance doc missing",
        "tests failing"
      ]
    },
    "no_circular_dependencies": {
      "name": "Dependency graph must be acyclic",
      "validation": "graph_analysis.check_no_cycles()",
      "applies_to": ["all"],
      "severity": "CRITICAL",
      "auto_block_merge": true
    }
  }
}
```

```markdown
# GitHub Actions Specification: ORGAN-IV Automation Stack

**Version:** 1.0  
**Target Implementation:** Week 2-3  
**Framework:** GitHub Actions (native, no external runners needed)  
**Deployment Location:** `orchestration-start-here` repo  

---

## Overview

Five core workflows automate the entire seven-organ system:

| Workflow | Trigger | Purpose | Latency |
|----------|---------|---------|---------|
| **validate-dependencies** | Every PR in any repo | Block merge if deps invalid | <2 min |
| **monthly-organ-audit** | Cron: 1st of month | Full system health check | ~15 min |
| **promote-repo** | Repo label + comment | Handle Theory→Art→Commerce promotions | <5 min |
| **publish-process** | Issue label in ORGAN-III | Automate ORGAN-V essay creation | On-demand |
| **distribute-content** | Issue label in ORGAN-V | Trigger POSSE/newsletter distribution | On-demand |

All workflows read from `registry.json` and `governance-rules.json` as the single source of truth.

---

## Architecture Pattern

### Data-Driven Workflows

**Every workflow follows this pattern:**

```
Trigger Event
    ↓
Read Central Registry (registry.json)
    ↓
Apply Governance Rules (governance-rules.json)
    ↓
Execute Actions (open PR, close issue, notify, etc.)
    ↓
Update Registry + Create Audit Trail
```

This ensures consistency: **logic lives in data files, not workflow code.**

### Reusable Actions

All workflows use these composable actions:

1. **fetch-registry** — Clone/update central registry
2. **validate-against-rules** — Check constraints
3. **notify-organs** — Cross-repo notifications
4. **update-dependencies** — Modify `.meta/` files
5. **log-event** — Audit trail

These live in `orchestration-start-here/.github/actions/` and are reusable across workflows.

---

## Workflow 1: validate-dependencies

**Purpose:** Prevent merging code that violates dependency rules  
**Trigger:** On PR opened/updated in ANY repo  
**Latency:** <2 minutes

### Setup Instructions

1. Create `.github/workflows/validate-dependencies.yml` in **EVERY** repo (use template):

```yaml
name: Validate Dependencies

on:
  pull_request:
    paths:
      - '.meta/dependencies.json'
      - 'package.json'
      - 'requirements.txt'
      - 'Cargo.toml'

jobs:
  validate:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v3
        with:
          fetch-depth: 0
      
      - name: Fetch Central Registry
        run: |
          curl -s https://raw.githubusercontent.com/organvm-iv-taxis/orchestration-start-here/main/registry.json \
            -o registry.json
      
      - name: Check Dependency Rules
        run: |
          # Pseudocode; real implementation in Python/Node
          python3 - <<'EOF'
          import json
          
          # Load registry and PR changes
          registry = json.load(open('registry.json'))
          current_repo = "${{ github.repository }}"
          
          # Extract dependencies from PR diff
          # (uses gh CLI to fetch diff)
          
          # Validate against rules:
          # 1. No circular dependencies
          # 2. Dependencies only flow downward in organ hierarchy
          # 3. Transitive depth <= 4
          
          if violations:
              print(f"FAILED: {violations}")
              exit(1)
          else:
              print("PASSED: All dependency rules satisfied")
              exit(0)
          EOF
      
      - name: Comment Results
        if: always()
        uses: actions/github-script@v6
        with:
          script: |
            const fs = require('fs');
            const results = fs.readFileSync('validation-results.txt', 'utf8');
            github.rest.issues.createComment({
              issue_number: context.issue.number,
              owner: context.repo.owner,
              repo: context.repo.repo,
              body: `## Dependency Validation\n\n${results}`
            });
```

2. **Deployment:** Copy this template to all 46 repos (automated via second workflow)

3. **Force as required status check:**
   - Settings → Branches → Branch protection rule
   - Require `validate-dependencies` to pass before merge

### Configuration

Create `.meta/dependencies.json` in every repo:

```json
{
  "repo_name": "my-great-engine",
  "organ": "ORGAN-I",
  "status": "ACTIVE",
  "dependencies": {
    "internal": {
      "depends_on": [
        {
          "repo": "recursive-engine--generative-entity",
          "org": "organvm-i-theoria",
          "organ": "ORGAN-I",
          "type": "hard"
        }
      ],
      "consumed_by": [
        {
          "repo": "core-engine",
          "org": "organvm-ii-poiesis",
          "organ": "ORGAN-II"
        }
      ]
    }
  }
}
```

### Success Criteria

- [ ] Circular dependency detected and blocked
- [ ] Downward dependency violations blocked
- [ ] Transitive depth violations detected
- [ ] Clear error message on failure
- [ ] Passes on valid PRs

## Workflow 2: monthly-organ-audit

**Purpose:** Full health check across all seven organs  
**Trigger:** Cron: `0 2 1 * *` (2 AM UTC on 1st of every month)  
**Latency:** ~15 minutes

### Implementation

**File:** `.github/workflows/monthly-organ-audit.yml` (in orchestration repo only)

```yaml
name: Monthly Organ Audit

on:
  schedule:
    - cron: '0 2 1 * * '  # 1st of month, 2 AM UTC
  workflow_dispatch:  # Manual trigger

jobs:
  audit:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v3
      
      - name: Setup Python
        uses: actions/setup-python@v4
        with:
          python-version: '3.11'
      
      - name: Run Organ Audit
        run: |
          python3 scripts/organ-audit.py \
            --registry registry.json \
            --governance governance-rules.json \
            --output audit-report.md
      
      - name: Generate Metrics
        run: |
          python3 scripts/calculate-metrics.py \
            --registry registry.json \
            --output metrics.json
      
      - name: Create GitHub Issue with Report
        uses: actions/github-script@v6
        with:
          script: |
            const fs = require('fs');
            const report = fs.readFileSync('audit-report.md', 'utf8');
            const metrics = JSON.parse(fs.readFileSync('metrics.json', 'utf8'));
            
            const body = `
            # Monthly Organ Audit — ${new Date().toISOString().split('T')[0]}
            
            ${report}
            
            ## System Metrics
            - Total repos: ${metrics.total_repos}
            - Operational organs: ${metrics.operational_organs}/7
            - Completion: ${metrics.completion}%
            - Critical alerts: ${metrics.critical_alerts}
            - Warnings: ${metrics.warnings}
            `;
            
            github.rest.issues.create({
              owner: context.repo.owner,
              repo: context.repo.repo,
              title: `Monthly Organ Audit — ${new Date().toISOString().split('T')[0]}`,
              body: body,
              labels: ['audit', 'monthly']
            });
      
      - name: Push Metrics to Registry
        run: |
          git config user.name "Orchestration Bot"
          git config user.email "bot@4444j99.orchestration"
          
          # Append metrics to registry history
          python3 - <<'EOF'
          import json
          from datetime import datetime
          
          registry = json.load(open('registry.json'))
          metrics = json.load(open('metrics.json'))
          
          registry['audit_history'] = registry.get('audit_history', [])
          registry['audit_history'].append({
            'date': datetime.now().isoformat(),
            'metrics': metrics
          })
          
          json.dump(registry, open('registry.json', 'w'), indent=2)
          EOF
          
          git add registry.json
          git commit -m "Monthly audit metrics — $(date +%Y-%m-%d)"
          git push
```

### Audit Script (Python)

**File:** `scripts/organ-audit.py`

```python
#!/usr/bin/env python3
import json
import sys
from datetime import datetime, timedelta

def audit_organs(registry_path, governance_path):
    """Run comprehensive system audit."""
    
    with open(registry_path) as f:
        registry = json.load(f)
    with open(governance_path) as f:
        governance = json.load(f)
    
    report = []
    alerts = {'critical': [], 'warning': []}
    
    # Audit each organ
    for organ_id in ['ORGAN-I', 'ORGAN-II', 'ORGAN-III', 'ORGAN-IV', 
                     'ORGAN-V', 'ORGAN-VI', 'ORGAN-VII']:
        organ = registry['organs'].get(organ_id, {})
        report.append(f"\n## {organ_id}: {organ.get('name', 'Unknown')}\n")
        
        # Check operational status
        status = organ.get('operational_status')
        completion = organ.get('completion', 0)
        report.append(f"**Status:** {status} ({completion}% complete)\n")
        
        # Run organ-specific checks
        if organ_id == 'ORGAN-I':
            report += check_theory_organ(organ, alerts)
        elif organ_id == 'ORGAN-II':
            report += check_art_organ(organ, alerts)
        elif organ_id == 'ORGAN-III':
            report += check_commerce_organ(organ, alerts)
        # ... etc
    
    # Validate dependency graph
    report += validate_dependency_graph(registry, alerts)
    
    # Check for alert conditions
    report.append(f"\n## Alerts\n")
    if alerts['critical']:
        report.append(f"🔴 **Critical ({len(alerts['critical'])}):**\n")
        for alert in alerts['critical']:
            report.append(f"- {alert}\n")
    
    if alerts['warning']:
        report.append(f"⚠️ **Warnings ({len(alerts['warning'])}):**\n")
        for alert in alerts['warning']:
            report.append(f"- {alert}\n")
    
    return ''.join(report), alerts

def validate_dependency_graph(registry, alerts):
    """Check for circular deps, broken links, etc."""
    report = ["\n## Dependency Validation\n"]
    
    # Build graph
    graph = {}
    for organ_id, organ in registry['organs'].items():
        for repo in organ.get('repositories', []):
            repo_name = repo['name']
            graph[repo_name] = {
                'deps': repo.get('relationships', {}).get('depends_on', []),
                'consumers': repo.get('relationships', {}).get('consumed_by', [])
            }
    
    # Check for cycles
    cycles = find_cycles(graph)
    if cycles:
        for cycle in cycles:
            alerts['critical'].append(f"Circular dependency: {' → '.join(cycle)}")
            report.append(f"🔴 Circular dep found: {cycle}\n")
    
    # Check for broken references
    for repo_name, deps in graph.items():
        for dep in deps['deps']:
            if dep not in graph:
                alerts['warning'].append(f"{repo_name} depends on missing {dep}")
    
    return report

if __name__ == '__main__':
    import argparse
    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser()
    parser.add_argument('--registry', required=True)
    parser.add_argument('--governance', required=True)
    parser.add_argument('--output', required=True)
    
    args = parser.parse_args()
    
    report, alerts = audit_organs(args.registry, args.governance)
    
    with open(args.output, 'w') as f:
        f.write(report)
    
    # Exit code based on critical alerts
    sys.exit(1 if alerts['critical'] else 0)
```

### Success Criteria

- [ ] Audit completes within 15 minutes
- [ ] Report generated with all organ status
- [ ] Critical alerts trigger GitHub issues
- [ ] Metrics recorded in audit history
- [ ] No false positives
