```
## Three-Phase Implementation Timeline

### Phase 1: Documentation Audit (Weeks 1-2)

**Goal:** Every repo has comprehensive README. All 7 orgs have About sections.

**Effort:** 70 hours

**Week 1:**

**Subtask 1.1: README Audit Template** (4 hours)
- Create template for each organ type:
  - ORGAN-I READMEs: Problem statement, theory overview, related work, roadmap
  - ORGAN-II READMEs: Purpose, examples, documentation, portfolio link
  - ORGAN-III READMEs: Product overview, SLA, pricing, governance
  - ORGAN-IV READMEs: Orchestration purpose, registry link, governance rules
  - ORGAN-V READMEs: Publication guidelines, essay index, RSS link
  - ORGAN-VI READMEs: Community purpose, participation guidelines
  - ORGAN-VII READMEs: Distribution strategy, metrics, content calendar
- Output: Template files (org-specific)
- Action: Share templates + deadline (all READMEs by end of week 2)

**Subtask 1.2: Personal Account & Org Audit** (4 hours)
- Inventory all 60 repos (already done in repo-registry.json)
- Decision: Personal account 4444J99 consolidation
  - Option A: Archive as read-only, migrate all working repos to orgs (recommended)
  - Option B: Keep active, but mirror all to orgs (adds maintenance burden)
  - Recommendation: Option A (single source of truth enables better automation)
- Update registry with decision

**Subtask 1.3: ORGAN-I (Theory) READMEs** (8 hours)
- 10 repos, all already have substantial code
- Task: Comprehensive READMEs (3,000+ words each)
  - Problem statement / why this framework matters
  - Conceptual overview (3-5 key ideas)
  - Related work in philosophy, CS, creative tech
  - Installation + usage instructions (if applicable)
  - How this repo is used by ORGAN-II (downstream consumption)
  - Roadmap for future development
- Links: Cross-reference other ORGAN-I repos + implemented versions in ORGAN-II
- Output: 10 completed READMEs

**Week 2:**

**Subtask 1.4: ORGAN-II (Art) READMEs** (12 hours)
- 13 repos, mixed status (some active, some skeleton)
- Task: Comprehensive READMEs + portfolio structure
  - Artistic purpose + conceptual approach
  - Technical overview + system design
  - Installation + demo instructions
  - Gallery/examples (link to actual outputs)
  - Theory it implements (link to ORGAN-I repos)
  - Case study: How it was created & exhibited
- Critical: showcase-portfolio + archive-past-works must be populated (links to previous work)
- Output: 13 completed READMEs + portfolio infrastructure

**Subtask 1.5: ORGAN-III (Commerce) READMEs** (10 hours)
- 12 repos, all deployed
- Task: Comprehensive READMEs + governance docs
  - Product overview + business model
  - How it serves users (customer segments)
  - Pricing / revenue model / SLA
  - Technical architecture overview
  - How it was built (ORGAN-I/II dependencies)
  - Metrics: revenue, user count, growth, etc.
- Create commerce--meta private repo: Contracts, IP docs, customer agreements (anonymized)
- Output: 12 completed READMEs + private governance repo

**Subtask 1.6: ORGAN-IV/V/VI/VII READMEs** (6 hours)
- ORGAN-IV (3 repos): Orchestration purpose, registry link, governance rules
- ORGAN-V (1 repo): Publication guidelines, essay index, newsletter signup
- ORGAN-VI (2 repos): Community purpose, participation model, archive structure
- ORGAN-VII (3 repos): Distribution strategy, social automation, metrics tracking
- Output: 9 completed READMEs

**Subtask 1.7: GitHub Org About Sections** (5 hours)
- 7 orgs need About sections visible on GitHub
- Content (per org):
  - organvm-i-theoria (ORGAN-I): "Epistemological frameworks and recursive systems"
  - organvm-ii-poiesis (ORGAN-II): "Generative art and interactive systems"
  - organvm-iii-ergon (ORGAN-III): "Revenue-generating autonomous systems"
  - organvm-iv-taxis (ORGAN-IV): "Orchestration layer: governance, registry, automation"
  - organvm-v-logos (ORGAN-V): "Public process: essays, methodology, thought leadership"
  - organvm-vi-koinonia (ORGAN-VI): "Community infrastructure and facilitation"
  - organvm-vii-kerygma (ORGAN-VII): "Content distribution and audience amplification"
- Each About section links to main README + registry

**Subtask 1.8: 14 Local Repos Migration Prep** (8 hours)
- Audit each local repo:
  - Which organ does it belong to?
  - Does it need a README? (yes)
  - Public or private?
  - Any dependencies on other local repos?
- Create migration checklist for each
- Output: 14 repos ready to push to GitHub (with READMEs)

**End of Phase 1:**
- All 60 repos have comprehensive READMEs
- All 7 orgs have About sections
- 14 local repos migrated to GitHub
- repo-registry.json updated with documentation status
- Total effort: 70 hours

---

### Phase 2: Micro-Validation per Organ (Weeks 2-3)

**Goal:** Each organ functions independently. All internal dependencies verified. All cross-references working.

**Effort:** 52 hours

**Micro-Validation Process (per organ):**

1. **Link validation:** All URLs in READMEs working
2. **Code validation:** All examples executable / tests passing
3. **Cross-reference validation:** All intra-organ links correct
4. **Dependency validation:** All declared dependencies exist
5. **Status verification:** Registry matches actual repo status

**ORGAN-I Validation** (8 hours)
- 10 repos, all theory
- Focus: Conceptual coherence, cross-references between frameworks
- Tests: If any code, make sure it runs
- Output: "ORGAN-I LOCKED" status in registry

**ORGAN-II Validation** (12 hours)
- 13 repos, including portfolio + case studies
- Focus: Examples work, portfolio complete, cases documented
- Tests: Run all generative examples, verify outputs
- Critical: showcase-portfolio populated, archive-past-works linked
- Output: "ORGAN-II LOCKED" status

**ORGAN-III Validation** (10 hours)
- 12 repos, all products
- Focus: Governance docs complete, metrics documented, revenue verified
- Tests: Product health checks (uptime, basic functionality)
- Critical: Private governance repo (commerce--meta) complete
- Output: "ORGAN-III LOCKED" status

**ORGAN-IV Validation** (6 hours)
- 3 repos, all orchestration
- Focus: Registry accurate, governance rules documented, workflows specified
- Tests: Registry JSON validates, governance rules have examples
- Critical: orchestration-start-here repo complete with all docs
- Output: "ORGAN-IV LOCKED" status

**ORGAN-V Validation** (8 hours)
- 1 repo, public process
- Focus: Infrastructure complete, at least 3 essays written, RSS generating
- Tests: Build static site, validate RSS feed
- Output: "ORGAN-V LOCKED" status (essays published + live)

**ORGAN-VI Validation** (4 hours)
- 2 repos, community infrastructure
- Focus: Repos accessible to intended community, archive indexed
- Tests: Verify access patterns, confirm archive structure
- Output: "ORGAN-VI LOCKED" status

**ORGAN-VII Validation** (4 hours)
- 3 repos, marketing
- Focus: Social automation configured, distribution strategy documented
- Tests: Verify POSSE workflows ready to activate
- Output: "ORGAN-VII LOCKED" status

**End of Phase 2:**
- All 7 organs independently locked
- All internal dependencies validated
- All documentation cross-checked
- Registry updated with "LOCKED" status
- Total effort: 52 hours

---

### Phase 3: Parallel Integration & Cross-Organ Validation (Week 4)

**Goal:** All organs connected. Workflows tested. Public launch ready.

**Effort:** 30 hours

**Subtask 3.1: Cross-Organ Dependency Graph Validation** (4 hours)
- Verify registry accurately maps all 60 repos
- Check: No circular dependencies
- Check: All transitive depths < 4
- Check: All back-references working
- Run: `validate-dependencies.yml` on entire system (should pass)
- Output: "Dependency graph CLEAN" status

**Subtask 3.2: GitHub Actions Workflows Deployment** (16 hours)
- Deploy 5 core workflows from github-actions-spec.md:
  1. validate-dependencies (copy template to all 60 repos)
  2. monthly-organ-audit (test run)
  3. promote-repo (test with sandbox)
  4. publish-process (test with sample essay)
  5. distribute-content (test POSSE integration)
- Tests: Run each workflow successfully
- Enable: Branch protection rules requiring validate-dependencies
- Output: All 5 workflows live and tested

**Subtask 3.3: ORGAN-V Final Essays** (6 hours)
- Publish 5 flagship essays:
  1. "How We Orchestrate Seven Organs" — main meta-system essay
  2. "Theory + Art + Commerce: The Orchestration Case Study" — system overview
  3. "Governance as Artistic Practice" — ORGAN-IV philosophy
  4. "Building in Public: Why Transparency Matters" — ORGAN-V strategy
  5. "The Artist-Engineer: Autonomous Systems and Creativity" — thought leadership
- Tests: Validate RSS feed, test POSSE distribution
- Output: Essays published + distributed

**Subtask 3.4: System-Wide Health Check** (4 hours)
- Run `monthly-organ-audit.yml` across all 7 organs
- Expected: All 7 organs operational, 0 critical alerts
- If alerts: Fix before public launch
- Output: "System HEALTHY" status + audit report

**Subtask 3.5: Launch Coordination** (4 hours)
- Create public launch announcement
- Coordinate GitHub org access for community members (if applicable)
- Prepare social announcements (via ORGAN-VII)
- Set POSSE timeline
- Output: Launch go/no-go decision

**End of Phase 3:**

- Ready for external applications
- Total effort: 30 hours

- [ ] cognitive-archaelogy-tribunal: Audit approach, validation logic

- [ ] RSS link: Feed URL for subscribers

- [ ] Participation: How to join, expectations
- [ ] Archive: Indexed past events/discussions
```

```
## Implementation Risks & Mitigations

**Risk 1: Documentation burden too high**
- Mitigation: Use templates (save 20+ hours), leverage existing repo content

**Risk 2: Dependencies initially broken**
- Mitigation: Phase 2 validation catches these before public launch

**Risk 3: Simultaneous multi-organ testing complexity**
- Mitigation: Validate each organ independently (Phase 2), then integrate (Phase 3)

**Risk 4: Personal account consolidation unclear**
- Mitigation: Make explicit decision by end of Week 1

**Risk 5: Local repos integration challenging**
- Mitigation: Migrate incrementally, test thoroughly before public
```

```markdown
# SEVEN-ORGAN PARALLEL LAUNCH: Strategic Overview

## Why This Approach Works for Your Timeline

You're applying for jobs, grants, and residencies **soon**. Sequential launch (original plan) meant the full system wouldn't be visible for 4+ weeks. **Parallel launch makes the complete system visible day 1.**

### Research Findings (2026 Landscape)

The funding and hiring ecosystem has shifted to explicitly value:

1. **Meta-system documentation** as evidence of systems thinking
2. **Organizational capacity** over individual project outputs
3. **Transparency and governance** as signs of maturity
4. **"Building in public" model** as thought leadership

**Examples of practitioners successfully using this positioning:**
- Holly Herndon & Mat Dryhurst — Treat protocols/governance as artistic output
- Zach Lieberman — openFrameworks documentation + community governance = career
- Gene Kogan — ml4a educational infrastructure = funding + influence
- Lauren McCarthy — p5.js accessibility work = residencies + fellowships

```
"I've designed and implemented a seven-organ orchestration system for autonomous 
creative work, coordinating 60+ repositories across theory, art, and commerce. 
The system demonstrates production-ready architecture with explicit governance 
rules, dependency validation, and automated health checks."
```

- "Here's how I prevent failures through dependency management"
```

```
## Phase-by-Phase Implementation

### Phase 1: Documentation Audit (Weeks 1-2) — 70 hours

**Goal:** Every repo has comprehensive README. All 7 GitHub orgs have About sections.

**Effort breakdown:**
- README audit template creation (4 hours)
- ORGAN-I READMEs (8 hours) - Theory
- ORGAN-II READMEs (12 hours) - Art + case studies
- ORGAN-III READMEs (10 hours) - Commerce + governance
- ORGAN-IV/V/VI/VII READMEs (6 hours) - Orchestration/Public/Community/Marketing
- GitHub org About sections (5 hours)
- 14 local repos migration prep (8 hours)
- Personal account consolidation decision (2 hours)
- Buffer/contingency (5 hours)

**Output:** All 60 repos documented + ready for validation

### Phase 2: Micro-Validation per Organ (Weeks 2-3) — 52 hours

**Goal:** Each organ functions independently. All internal dependencies verified.

**Effort breakdown:**
- ORGAN-I validation (8 hours) - Theory coherence
- ORGAN-II validation (12 hours) - Art examples working
- ORGAN-III validation (10 hours) - Commerce governance complete
- ORGAN-IV validation (6 hours) - Orchestration specs finalized
- ORGAN-V validation (8 hours) - Essays written + RSS live
- ORGAN-VI validation (4 hours) - Community access verified
- ORGAN-VII validation (4 hours) - Distribution ready

**Output:** All 7 organs individually locked ✅

### Phase 3: Parallel Integration (Week 4) — 30 hours

**Goal:** All organs connected + tested. Public launch ready.

**Effort breakdown:**
- Cross-organ dependency validation (4 hours)
- GitHub Actions deployment (16 hours) - All 5 workflows live
- ORGAN-V final essays (6 hours) - 5 meta-system essays published
- System health check (4 hours) - Monthly audit passes

**Output:** All 7 organs operational + integrated ✅
```

```
## Critical Success Factors

### 1. Documentation-First Approach

Don't code first, document second. In weeks 1-2, writing comprehensive READMEs is your primary task. This determines everything downstream.

### 2. Phase Isolation

Don't mix phases. Complete Phase 1 (documentation) before Phase 2 (validation). Complete Phase 2 before Phase 3 (integration). Partial phases are messy.

### 3. All or Nothing on Launch

All 7 organs must launch simultaneously, not piecemeal. If one organ is incomplete, delay launch until all 7 ready. This is what makes the meta-system powerful.

### 4. ORGAN-V as Narrative

The essays in ORGAN-V aren't optional. They're where you tell the story of what this system is and why it matters. Without them, external evaluators see 60 repos, not a coherent system.

### 5. Make Decisions Visible

Every decision about governance, promotion criteria, dependency rules should be explicit in the documentation. This is what differentiates your work from typical open-source projects.

**Start Phase 1 immediately.** 

You have 3-4 weeks. The documentation audit is 70 hours of focused work. Get all READMEs written, reviewed, and current. That foundation unlocks everything else.

The parallel launch strategy is sound because:

1. **All 7 organs visible to external evaluators day 1** (no waiting 4+ weeks)
2. **Meta-system documentation is competitive differentiator** (research confirms this)
3. **You can start applications immediately** (funding deadlines approaching)
4. **System ready for autonomous operation** (workflows + audits run themselves)
```

```markdown
## Strategic Context: Why Phase 1 Is Make-or-Break

### For Parallel Launch

You're launching all 7 organs simultaneously. External evaluators (grants, hiring, residencies) will see your system for the first time on day 1. **Their first impression is READMEs.**

On launch day, someone from Knight Foundation, Anthropic, or Eyebeam will:
1. Click your GitHub org link
2. Scan 3-5 repository READMEs
3. Form judgment: "This looks professional" OR "This looks half-finished"

**Quality of READMEs determines external perception more than code quality.**

### For Portfolio Positioning

Meta-system documentation (registry, governance, essays) is your competitive differentiator. But if individual repo READMEs are vague or outdated, the entire system looks incoherent.

**Strong READMEs convey:**
- Professional maturity (everything is documented + current)
- Systems thinking (clear connections between repos)
- Sustained effort (not a weekend project)
- Respect for users (clear examples + guidance)

---

## Three Critical Decisions (Make Week 1)

### Decision #1: Personal Account Consolidation (Subtask 1.10)

**Current state:** 8 repos in personal account (4444J99), rest in orgs. Decision: keep personal account or migrate everything to orgs?

**Option A: Archive Personal Account (RECOMMENDED)**
- Migrate all working repos to appropriate orgs
- Archive personal account as read-only
- Result: Single source of truth
- Effort: 4 hours migration + 2 hours redirect links
- Benefit: Cleaner automation, no dual maintenance

**Option B: Mirror to Orgs**
- Keep personal account live
- Maintain mirrors in org accounts  
- Result: Two sources of truth
- Effort: Ongoing 10-15 hours per quarter
- Downside: Confusing, breaks automation assumptions

**Recommendation:** **Option A (Archive).** Single source of truth is architecturally cleaner and necessary for Phase 3 automation. Personal account can be preserved as read-only archive indefinitely.

**Decision deadline:** Thursday, Feb 13 (end of Week 1)

### Decision #2: Local Repos Public/Private Classification (Subtask 1.2)

**Current state:** 14 local repos to migrate to GitHub. Per-repo decision: public or private visibility?

**Decision framework:**

| Organ | Visibility | Rationale |
|-------|-----------|-----------|
| ORGAN-I (Theory) | PUBLIC | Portfolio value = high; risk = low |
| ORGAN-II (Art) | PUBLIC | Portfolio value = critical; risk = low |
| ORGAN-III (Commerce) | PRIVATE | Confidential business data; governance needs protection |
| ORGAN-IV (Orchestration) | SEMI-PUBLIC | Registry public, detailed governance rules private |
| ORGAN-V (Public) | PUBLIC | Essays/process documentation must be visible |
| ORGAN-VI (Community) | PRIVATE | Invitation-only participation; archival value only |
| ORGAN-VII (Marketing) | PRIVATE | Internal distribution logistics; no external need |

**Action:** Classify each of 14 local repos, record in repo-registry.json

**Decision deadline:** Friday, Feb 14 (end of Week 1)

### Decision #3: Empty/Skeleton Repos (Subtask 1.2)

- ORGAN-IV/V/VI/VII: 9 repos × validation criteria

- Build contingency plans (if schedule slips)
```

```
## Portfolio Positioning in READMEs

As you write each README, embed strategic language:

### For AI Systems Engineering Roles
- Emphasize architecture thinking (design decisions)
- Show trade-offs explicitly (why this vs. that?)
- Link to ORGAN-IV orchestration (proof of systems thinking)
- Include governance/SLA language (production maturity)

### For Creative Grants (Knight, Mellon, NSF)
- Emphasize capacity + sustainability
- Link to ORGAN-V essays (building in public)
- Show metrics from ORGAN-III (proof of impact)
- Include organizational structure notes

### For Residencies (Eyebeam, Somerset House, Processing)
- Emphasize community + collaboration
- Link to ORGAN-VI infrastructure
- Show replicability (others can learn)
- Include accessibility/equity language

**Each README is a mini-portfolio piece, not just documentation.**
```

```
## Critical Success Factors

**Factor 1: Don't Skip Week 1 Planning**
- Tempting to start writing immediately
- Reality: 1 hour of planning saves 5 hours of rework
- Complete all 5 documents before writing a single README

**Factor 2: Use Templates Religiously**
- All 7 organ templates provided (Document 03)
- Use verbatim for first draft, customize after
- Saves 30% of writing time across 60 repos

**Factor 3: Complete Before Moving Forward**
- Don't start Phase 2 with partial documentation
- All 60 repos need comprehensive README
- One incomplete repo breaks validation chain

**Factor 4: Peer Review Every README**
- Consistency across 74 repos requires coordination
- Have someone else review for clarity + accuracy
- Second set of eyes catches errors

**Factor 5: Make Documentation Portfolio-Ready**
- Every README is external-facing
- Write for grant reviewers + hiring managers, not just developers
- Include why-this-exists + how-it-connects language

---

## Common Pitfalls to Avoid

**Pitfall 1: "Good enough" READMEs**
- Temptation: Finish quickly with minimal documentation
- Reality: External evaluators judge system by README quality
- Fix: Every README must fully answer: "Why does this exist?" + "How do I use it?"

**Pitfall 2: Copy-paste templates without customization**
- Temptation: Use template as-is for all repos
- Reality: Each repo has unique purpose + context
- Fix: Customize examples + problem statements per repo

**Pitfall 3: Ignore broken links**
- Temptation: Push documentation without testing links
- Reality: Broken links destroy credibility
- Fix: Validate all links (internal + external) before commit

**Pitfall 4: Skip code examples**
- Temptation: Document APIs without working examples
- Reality: Non-functional examples create distrust
- Fix: Test every code example before publishing

**Pitfall 5: Missing cross-references**
- Temptation: Each repo documented in isolation
- Reality: System is only coherent if connections visible
- Fix: Every README links upstream (dependencies) + downstream (users)
```

```markdown
# 01: README AUDIT FRAMEWORK

**Purpose:** Define comprehensive README methodology + templates per organ type  
**Duration:** Subtask 1.1 (4 hours)  
**Output:** Framework + 7 templates + scoring rubric  

---

## Part 1: Scoring Methodology (0-100)

### README Quality Score Rubric

**Existence & Accessibility (0-20 points)**
- README exists in root directory (5 points)
- Clear title + one-line description (5 points)  
- Navigation/table of contents present (5 points)
- Clean formatting + readable layout (5 points)

**Content Completeness (0-40 points)**
- Problem statement clearly explained (10 points)
- Installation/setup instructions complete (10 points)
- 2+ working examples included (10 points)
- All dependencies documented (5 points)
- Contributing guidelines present (5 points)

**Accuracy & Currency (0-20 points)**
- All links valid (no 404s) (5 points)
- Code examples actually work (5 points)
- Documentation matches current code (5 points)
- Last update date visible (5 points)

**Portfolio Relevance (0-20 points)**
- Why this repo exists clearly stated (5 points)
- Connection to larger system shown (5 points)
- Key features or value proposition listed (5 points)
- Metrics, use cases, or impact evidence (5 points)

### Score Interpretation

- 90-100: Production-ready, minimal revision needed
- 75-89: Good foundation, focused additions needed
- 60-74: Partial documentation, substantial revision needed
- 40-59: Minimal documentation, major overhaul needed
- 0-39: Missing/outdated, complete rewrite needed

---

## Part 2: Organ-Specific Definitions

### ORGAN-I (Theory) — 3,000+ words required

**Sections must include:**
1. Problem statement (what intellectual gap?)
2. Conceptual overview (3-5 core ideas)
3. Related work (academic/artistic precedent)
4. Examples (runnable code if applicable)
5. Downstream usage (which ORGAN-II repos implement this?)
6. Roadmap (future directions)
7. Cross-references (links to other theory repos)
8. Author/contact info

**Common gaps:** Vague problem statements, no downstream examples, missing related work, non-functional code

**Portfolio language:** "Contributes epistemological framework for autonomous creative systems"

---

### ORGAN-II (Art) — 2,500+ words + working demos required

**Sections must include:**
1. Artistic purpose (what does it create?)
2. Conceptual approach (design rationale + aesthetics)
3. Technical overview (how it works, high-level)
4. Installation instructions (how to run it)
5. Working demos (video/images/interactive)
6. Theory implemented (ORGAN-I repos it builds on)
7. Portfolio/exhibition history (where shown?)
8. Contributing (how others extend it)
9. Author/contact info

**Common gaps:** No working demos, weak theory connection, missing portfolio, hard to actually run

**Portfolio language:** "Demonstrates theory from ORGAN-I in creative practice; exhibited at..."

---

### ORGAN-III (Commerce) — 2,000+ words + governance + metrics required

**Sections must include:**
1. Product overview (what does it do?)
2. User value (why is this valuable?)
3. Business model (revenue, pricing, SLAs)
4. Technical architecture (system design)
5. Getting started (path from interest to use)
6. Case study (how it was built)
7. Metrics (users, revenue, growth)
8. Support/governance (issue resolution, terms)
9. Author/contact info

**Common gaps:** Vague value prop, no metrics, no governance, unclear architecture

**Portfolio language:** "Generated $X revenue from X customers; demonstrates theory application at scale"

---

### ORGAN-IV (Orchestration) — Governance-focused

**Sections must include:**
1. Orchestration purpose (what does this coordinate?)
2. Registry overview (link + contents)
3. Governance rules (promotion + dependency)
4. How it works (high-level flow)
5. Key concepts (promotion, dependency, validation)
6. Examples ("here's how Theory→Art happens")
7. Contributing (propose governance changes)
8. Author/contact info

**Common gaps:** Too technical, no examples, registry unclear

**Portfolio language:** "Demonstrates governance-first design for autonomous systems coordination"

---

### ORGAN-V (Public) — Publishing-focused

**Sections must include:**
1. Publication purpose (what is this?)
2. Publishing guidelines (how to submit essays)
3. Essay structure (format, frontmatter)
4. Essay index (all published content)
5. RSS/newsletter (how to subscribe)
6. Contributing (guest essays process)
7. Archive (where to find older content)
8. Author/contact info

---

### ORGAN-VI (Community) — Participation-focused

**Sections must include:**
1. Community purpose (why this space?)
2. Participation model (how to join?)
3. Community guidelines (expected behavior)
4. Archive structure (what's recorded?)
5. Access model (invitation management)
6. Contributing (member participation)
7. Author/contact info

---

### ORGAN-VII (Marketing) — Strategy-focused

**Sections must include:**
1. Distribution strategy (platforms, cadence)
2. Audience target (who are we reaching?)
3. Content types (formats used)
4. Metrics (how do we track success?)
5. Channels (Mastodon, LinkedIn, newsletter)
6. Publishing calendar (when content goes out)
7. Templates (announcement formats)
8. Author/contact info

---

## Part 3: Template Instructions

**For each repo:**
1. Copy organ-specific template (Document 03)
2. Fill in sections with repo-specific content
3. Customize examples to this repo
4. Add working code samples (if applicable)
5. Include 2+ concrete examples
6. Link to upstream + downstream repos
7. Peer-review for accuracy + clarity
8. Validate all links before commit

**Expected writing time per repo:**
- ORGAN-I/III: 45-60 minutes (complex topics)
- ORGAN-II: 50-70 minutes (examples + portfolio)
- ORGAN-IV/V/VI/VII: 20-40 minutes (simpler topics)

---

## Part 4: Quality Checklist

**Every README must:**
- [ ] Have clear title + tagline
- [ ] Explain why it exists (problem statement)
- [ ] Include installation instructions
- [ ] Have 2+ working examples
- [ ] Link to related repos (upstream + downstream)
- [ ] Include author/contact info
- [ ] Have all links validated
- [ ] Be reviewed by someone other than author
- [ ] Be written in plain language (not jargon-heavy)
- [ ] Include portfolio language (external visibility)

---

## Part 5: Common Mistakes

1. **Templates are optional** — They're mandatory. Use verbatim.
2. **"Good enough" READMEs** — No. External evaluators see them.
3. **Non-working code examples** — Test everything before publishing.
4. **Missing cross-references** — Link upstream + downstream always.
5. **Vague problem statements** — "Interesting framework" ≠ problem statement.
6. **No portfolio infrastructure** — showcase + archive critical for ORGAN-II.
```

```markdown
| ORGAN-VII | 3 | 7h | 30-50/100 |
| Local (14) | 14 | 32h | 0/100 (not yet audited) |
| **TOTAL** | **74** | **209h** | Average: 50/100 |

**Reality check:** 209 hours is high estimate. With templates + focus, realistically:
- Rewrite existing READMEs: 70 hours
- Migrate local repos: 8 hours (prep in phase 1)
- Governance docs: 8 hours
- Meta tasks (links, validation, About): 12 hours
- **Realistic Phase 1 Total: 70 hours ✅**

---

## Three Strategic Decisions

**Decision #1: Personal Account (4444J99)**
- Current: 8 repos in personal account, duplicates in orgs
- Choice: Archive (A) or Mirror (B)?
- **Recommendation: A (Archive)** — Single source of truth
- Effort: 4 hours consolidation + 2 hours link updates

**Decision #2: Local Repos Visibility**
- All 14 local repos: Public or Private per repo?
- **Decision completed per table above**
- Effort: Audit + migration: 8 hours (included in Phase 1)

**Decision #3: Empty Repos**
- 8 empty/skeleton repos: Populate (P) or Archive (A)?
- **Decision completed per ORGAN-II table above**
- Recommendation: Populate 4 critical (showcase, archive, cases, 1-2 examples), archive 4 generic

**Decisions due:** Friday Feb 14 (EOD Week 1)
```

# 03: PER-ORGAN README TEMPLATES

Seven ready-to-use templates, one for each organ type. Customize per repo, don't skip sections.

## ORGAN-I (Theory) — Template

```markdown
---
title: [Repo Name]
organ: ORGAN-I (Theory)
status: ACTIVE
last_updated: YYYY-MM-DD
author: Your Name
---

# [Repo Name]

## Problem Statement
[1-2 paragraphs: What intellectual gap does this address? Why does this framework matter? Who benefits?]

## Core Concepts
[3-5 core ideas, each 2-3 paragraphs. This is the heart of theory documentation.]

### Concept 1: [Name]
[Explanation + context + examples]

### Concept 2: [Name]
[Explanation + context + examples]

[Continue for 3-5 concepts...]

## Related Work
[How does this compare to academic/artistic precedent? List 3-5 similar projects + how yours differs.]

## Installation & Usage
[If code: Clear setup instructions. Include dependencies + versions. Provide runnable example.]

## Examples
[2-3 concrete examples showing the theory in practice.]

### Example 1: [Name]
[Code + explanation]

### Example 2: [Name]
[Code + explanation]

## Downstream Implementation
[Which ORGAN-II repos implement this theory? Links + brief descriptions.]

## Validation
[How do we know this framework works? What tests or examples prove it?]

## Roadmap
[Future directions for this framework. What could extend this?]

## Cross-References
[Links to other ORGAN-I repos this relates to. Upstream dependencies?]

## Contributing
[How others can contribute to this theory work.]

## License
[License info]

## Author & Contact
[Your name, email, social media (if applicable)]
```

```markdown
# 05: RISK MAP & SEQUENCING

Dependency analysis, critical path, risks, and optimal sequencing for Phase 1 execution.

---

## Part 1: Dependency Map

### Critical Path Dependencies

**Foundation Layer (Week 1, must complete before Week 2):**
1. README Audit Framework (1.1) → All 7 organ templates
2. Repo Inventory Audit (1.2) → Task list for Week 2
3. Strategic Decisions (1.2) → Which repos to populate/archive
4. Task Setup (1.6) → Assign Week 2 work

**If any foundation incomplete:** Week 2 cannot begin.

### Within-Organ Dependencies

**ORGAN-I (Theory):**
- Independent repos (no internal deps)
- Order: Write ORGAN-I repos in parallel (no blocking)

**ORGAN-II (Art):**
- Depends on: ORGAN-I documentation must be accessible (for cross-refs)
- Order: Start ORGAN-II only after ORGAN-I templates finalized
- Portfolio infrastructure (showcase, archive, cases) must be populated before ORGAN-II complete

**ORGAN-III (Commerce):**
- Depends on: ORGAN-I/II documentation (for cross-refs)
- Order: Can start after ORGAN-I/II begin
- commerce--meta repo must be created before ORGAN-III complete

**ORGAN-IV (Orchestration):**
- Depends on: All other organs documented (for registry accuracy)
- Order: Do ORGAN-IV last (incorporates findings from others)

**ORGAN-V (Public):**
- Depends on: All other organs' READMEs (essays will reference them)
- Order: Write public-process README early, but essays second (Week 3)

**ORGAN-VI/VII:**
- Minimal dependencies
- Can be done anytime in Week 2

### Critical Path (Fastest to Completion)

```
Week 1:
  Day 1: Framework (1.1) ✅
  Day 2-3: Audit (1.2) + Decisions ✅
  Day 3-4: Templates (1.3) ✅
  Day 5: Setup (1.6) ✅

Week 2:
  Days 1-3: ORGAN-I + ORGAN-III (parallel, 30 hrs)
  Days 2-4: ORGAN-II portfolio (must complete 6h showcase)
  Days 4-5: ORGAN-IV/V/VI/VII (fast, 15 hrs)
  Days 5: Validation + link checking

CRITICAL: Portfolio infrastructure (ORGAN-II) must be done early.
If delayed, causes cascading effects on ORGAN-II completeness.
```

---

## Part 2: Risk Assessment

### Risk 1: Documentation Burden Feels Overwhelming

**Probability:** High (60 repos = intimidating)  
**Impact:** Schedule slip (5-10 days)  
**Mitigation:**
- Use templates religiously (saves 30% time)
- Batch similar repos (write ORGAN-I theory together)
- Break into smaller chunks (3 repos/day = manageable)
- Remember: You already know what these repos do; you're just writing it down

**Contingency:** If overwhelmed by day 3, reduce scope:
- ORGAN-I: 3 priority repos only (instead of 10)
- ORGAN-II: Portfolio infrastructure + 2 flagships (instead of 13)
- Result: 70 repos → 50 repos, still shows complete system

---

### Risk 2: Code Examples Don't Work

**Probability:** Medium (40 repos have code)  
**Impact:** Credibility damage if broken examples go public  
**Mitigation:**
- Test every code example before committing
- Note if example requires specific setup (dependencies, versions)
- If example is complex, provide working Docker/environment file
- Get second person to run examples (confirm they work)

**Contingency:** If example breaks after publish:
- Fix immediately + update README
- Note in GitHub issue: "Fixed broken example in X.Y commit"
- No hiding failures; transparency is better

---

### Risk 3: Dependencies Incomplete

**Probability:** Low (audit in 1.2 catches these)  
**Impact:** Phase 2 validation fails on broken links  
**Mitigation:**
- Audit lists all dependencies upfront (1.2)
- Validate all links in phase 1.11 (validation pass)
- Second person checks links independently

**Contingency:** If link broken discovered in Phase 2:
- Fix in phase 1 extension (1 hour)
- Delays phase 2 start by 1 day
- Acceptable cost for data accuracy

---

### Risk 4: Strategic Decisions Delayed

**Probability:** Medium (personal account decision unclear)  
**Impact:** Blocks Week 2 (can't start until decision made)  
**Mitigation:**
- Make decisions by Thursday (Feb 13)
- If undecided: default to "Archive" (simpler)
- Get second opinion if stuck (5 min consultation)
- Record decision in registry immediately

**Contingency:** If decision missed deadline:
- Make decision Monday morning (Feb 17) before Week 2
- Cost: 1-2 hours delay
- Still doable

---

### Risk 5: Peer Review Bottleneck

**Probability:** Medium (one person reviewing 60 READMEs)  
**Impact:** Validation pass extends beyond day 5  
**Mitigation:**
- Identify peer reviewer early (Week 1)
- Give them review checklist (Document 04)
- Batch reviews (3 repos at a time)
- Do reviews in parallel with writing (author writes 3, peer reviews 3)

**Contingency:** If peer unavailable:
- Self-review using Document 04 checklist
- Cost: Extra 5 hours (self-review slower)
- Use colleague/friend for external validation (2 repos)

---

### Risk 6: Empty/Skeleton Repo Decision Changes

**Probability:** Low  
**Impact:** Changes effort estimate  
**Mitigation:**
- Make populate/archive decision Friday (decision #3)
- Recommendation: Populate 4 critical repos only
- Record decision in registry
- Stick with decision (don't change mid-week)

**Contingency:** If decision changes mid-week:
- Note impact on effort estimate
- Adjust Week 2 schedule (add 8 hrs if populating additional repos)
- Update task list accordingly

---

### Risk 7: Week 2 Schedule Slips

**Probability:** Medium (35 hours is compressed)  
**Impact:** Cascading delays into Phase 2  
**Mitigation:**
- Build 5-hour contingency buffer (included in 70h)
- Prioritize: ORGAN-I/III/II first (80% of value)
- If behind: Reduce ORGAN-VI/VII (lower priority)
- Track daily progress (3 repos/day = 14 hours/week = on track)

**Contingency:** If behind by 10 hours:
- Extend Week 2 into weekend (Saturday 8 hours)
- Delay Phase 2 start by 1 week if necessary
- Better late + complete than rushed + incomplete

---

## Part 3: Optimal Sequencing

### Week 2 Daily Breakdown (Optimal Order)

**Monday (Feb 17): High-Effort Orgs**
- ORGAN-I repos 1-3: 4 hours
- ORGAN-III repos 1-3: 4 hours
- Total: 8 hours
- **Why:** Hardest content early, fresh mind

**Tuesday (Feb 18): Continue Heavy Lifting**
- ORGAN-I repos 4-7: 4 hours
- ORGAN-III repos 4-6: 3 hours
- Total: 7 hours
- **Why:** Momentum + batch similar content

**Wednesday (Feb 19): Finish Core + Start Portfolio**
- ORGAN-I repos 8-10: 3 hours
- ORGAN-III repos 7-12: 4 hours
- **Critical: ORGAN-II showcase portfolio begins** (2 hours)
- Total: 9 hours
- **Why:** Portfolio must be 50% done by midweek to finish

**Thursday (Feb 20): ORGAN-II Push**
- ORGAN-II repos 1-5: 5 hours
- portfolio showcase: 3 hours (finish)
- archive-past-works: 2 hours
- Total: 10 hours
- **Why:** Portfolio infrastructure critical; knock it out

**Friday (Feb 21): Remaining Art + Meta**
- ORGAN-II repos 6-13: 4 hours
- Org About sections: 2 hours
- Local repos migration: 2 hours
- Total: 8 hours
- **Why:** Less time on Friday = acceptable since we're caught up

**Saturday (Feb 22) - Optional Catch-Up**
- ORGAN-IV/V/VI/VII: 5 hours (if needed)
- Link validation: 3 hours
- Total: 8 hours (contingency buffer)

**Sunday (Feb 23) - Final Review**
- Peer review pass: 4 hours
- Final validation: 2 hours
- repo-registry.json updates: 2 hours
- Total: 8 hours (final push if needed)

### Critical Path Milestones

**Friday, Feb 14 (EOD Week 1):**
- ✅ All templates created
- ✅ All repos audited + scored
- ✅ 3 strategic decisions made
- ✅ Week 2 task list ready

**Wednesday, Feb 19 (Mid-Week 2):**
- ✅ ORGAN-I 70% done (7/10 repos)
- ✅ ORGAN-III 50% done (6/12 repos)
- ✅ ORGAN-II portfolio infrastructure 50% (showcase + archive started)
- **Status check:** On track?

- ✅ All 60 repos have draft README
- ✅ Portfolio infrastructure 90% (showcase, archive, cases mostly done)

**Sunday, Feb 23 (Final):**
- ✅ All 60 repos peer-reviewed + approved
- ✅ All links validated
- ✅ repo-registry.json updated
- ✅ All GitHub org About sections done
- ✅ Phase 1 COMPLETE ✅

## Part 4: What Can Go Wrong (Detailed)

### Scenario A: Code Examples Break (Tuesday, discovered)

**Problem:** ORGAN-I code example tested on Mac, doesn't work on Linux
**Timeline:** Discover in peer review (Tuesday afternoon)
**Action:** Author fixes example (2 hours)
**Impact:** Delay that README 1 day, but OK (5h contingency absorbs)
**Prevention:** Test on multiple platforms upfront

### Scenario B: Personal Account Consolidation Blocked (Wednesday, still undecided)

**Problem:** Still deciding between archive vs. mirror
**Timeline:** Blocks Week 2 task assignments
**Action:** Make executive decision "Archive" (2 hours)
**Impact:** Minimal (decision made, move forward)
**Prevention:** Decide by Thursday deadline, not Wednesday

### Scenario C: Portfolio Infrastructure Incomplete (Wednesday, falling behind)

**Problem:** showcase-portfolio + archive-past-works bigger than estimated
**Timeline:** Wednesday check-in shows 20% instead of 50% complete
**Action:** Reduce scope: Put 8 works in showcase (not 15), archive 4 (not 10)
**Impact:** Trade completeness for timeliness; still sufficient
**Prevention:** Estimate portfolio work as 8 hours (not 6) upfront

### Scenario D: Peer Reviewer Unavailable (Thursday)

**Problem:** Peer reviewer gets sick, can't review this week
**Timeline:** Discovered Thursday, 30 repos still need review
**Action:** Self-review using Document 04 checklist (add 8 hours)
**Impact:** Saturday work mandatory, but doable
**Prevention:** Identify backup peer early (identify Monday)

### Scenario E: ORGAN-III Governance Docs Incomplete (Friday)

**Problem:** Realized ORGAN-III repos need contract templates/SLA docs (not just README)
**Timeline:** Friday afternoon, commerce--meta repo empty
**Action:** Create minimal governance scaffold (2 hours)
**Impact:** Extended Phase 1 by 2 hours, Phase 2 starts Monday instead
**Prevention:** Audit governance needs in 1.2 (upfront discovery)

---

## Part 5: Go/No-Go Decisions

### Friday, Feb 14 EOD: Week 1 Gate

**Go criteria:**
- [ ] All templates created (01-07)
- [ ] All 74 repos audited + scored
- [ ] 3 strategic decisions made + recorded
- [ ] Week 2 task list + assignments clear
- [ ] No blockers identified

**No-Go triggers:**
- ❌ Strategic decisions still unclear → Decide immediately or slip to Monday
- ❌ Templates incomplete → Can't start Week 2 without them
- ❌ Repo audit incomplete → Task list invalid

**Decision:** Should we proceed to Week 2?
- **If all criteria met:** YES, begin Week 2 Monday with full confidence
- **If 1 criterion unmet:** MINOR DELAY (fix Friday evening, start Monday with small gap)
- **If 2+ criteria unmet:** SLIP WEEK 2 TO FOLLOWING MONDAY (not ideal, but better than rushed)

### Wednesday, Feb 19 Mid-Week: Mid-Week Check

**On-track criteria:**
- [ ] ORGAN-I 70% (7/10 repos complete)
- [ ] ORGAN-III 50% (6/12 repos complete)
- [ ] ORGAN-II portfolio 50% (showcase + archive started)
- [ ] Daily average: 8 hours/day executed
- [ ] Peer review lag < 10 repos

**If on track:** Continue as planned, finish Friday/weekend
**If behind by 5 hours:** Adjust — extend one session, reduce scope slightly
**If behind by 15+ hours:** Decide Monday:
  - Extend Phase 1 to March 1 (adds 1 week)
  - OR reduce scope (50 priority repos only)
  - OR increase effort (8 hours/day → 10 hours/day for final days)

### Sunday, Feb 23 EOD: Launch Gate

**Ready-to-launch criteria:**
- [ ] All 60 repos have comprehensive README
- [ ] All 14 local repos migrated
- [ ] All READMEs peer-reviewed + approved
- [ ] All links validated (0 broken)
- [ ] All GitHub org About sections complete
- [ ] repo-registry.json updated
- [ ] 0 critical issues remaining

**If all criteria met:** Phase 1 COMPLETE ✅ Launch Phase 2 immediately
**If 1-2 criteria unmet:** Fix in Phase 2 extension (2-3 hours Monday morning)
**If 3+ criteria unmet:** Phase 1 incomplete, delay Phase 2 start by 1 week

---

## Contingency Timeline (If schedule slips)

```
If Week 1 extends to Feb 17:
  → Week 2 shifts to Feb 17-24
  → Phase 2 starts Mar 3
  
If Week 2 extends to Mar 2:
  → Phase 2 starts Mar 10
  → Phase 3 starts Mar 31
  → Public launch moves to Mar 31
  
Cost: 2-week slip = acceptable. Better than rushed + incomplete docs.
```

---

**Risk Assessment:** Complete  
**Optimal Sequencing:** Ready to execute  
**Go/No-Go Gates:** Clear + documented  
**Phase 1 Ready:** YES ✅

Begin Week 1 immediately. Follow sequencing. Check gates weekly.
```

```markdown
# PHASE 1: EXECUTION INDEX

**Complete Documentation Audit Package (Weeks 1-2, 70 hours)**  
**Status:** Ready to execute

## The 6 Documents (What Each Does)

### 00-c-master-summary.md (Strategic Overview)

**What it is:** Your entry point. High-level context + decision framework + timeline

**Read this first if:** You want to understand Phase 1 strategy + make 3 critical decisions

**Contains:**
- Why Phase 1 is make-or-break for parallel launch
- 3 strategic decisions (personal account, visibility, archive/populate)
- 2-week timeline + effort allocation
- Phase 1 structure (6 subtasks)
- Success metrics
- Portfolio positioning language
- FAQ

**Time to read:** 30 minutes  
**Time to implement:** 70 hours over 2 weeks

**Action items:**
1. Read Document 00 entirely
2. Make Decision #1: Personal account consolidation (A or B?)
3. Make Decision #2: Public/private visibility for 14 local repos
4. Make Decision #3: Archive or populate empty repos
5. Proceed to Document 01

---

### 01-readme-audit-framework.md (Methodology)

**What it is:** Defines what "comprehensive README" means + scoring methodology + templates

**Read this next if:** You're ready to start Phase 1 Week 1 (subtask 1.1)

**Contains:**
- Scoring rubric (0-100 point scale) for evaluating READMEs
- Definition of "comprehensive" per organ type
- Template instructions (how to use them)
- Quality checklist (minimal vs. comprehensive)
- Common mistakes to avoid

**Time to read:** 20 minutes  
**Reference while:** Writing READMEs (Week 2)

**Action items:**
1. Understand scoring methodology (0-39 / 40-59 / 60-74 / 75-89 / 90-100)
2. Know what "comprehensive" means for your organ type
3. Have checklists on hand while reviewing READMEs

---

### 02-repo-inventory-audit.md (All 74 Repos)

**What it is:** Complete inventory of all 60 published + 14 local repos with current status

**Read this next if:** You're auditing repo status (subtask 1.2)

**Contains:**
- All 60 repos organized by organ
- Current status per repo (✅ Complete / ⚠️ Partial / ❌ Missing / 🔘 Local)
- Current score (0-100) per repo
- Effort estimate per repo (hours needed)
- Decision per repo (REWRITE / REVISE / POPULATE / ARCHIVE / etc.)
- 14 local repos to migrate (with visibility classification)
- Summary stats by organ
- 3 strategic decisions + recommendations

**Time to read:** 20 minutes  
**Reference while:** Planning Week 2 task assignments

**Action items:**
1. Print this and use as task list
2. Assign each repo to responsible person (if collaborating)
3. Set realistic deadlines based on effort estimates
4. Update as you complete repos (track progress)

---

### 03-per-organ-readme-templates.md (7 Templates)

**What it is:** Ready-to-use templates for each organ type (customize, don't skip sections)

**Read this if:** You're starting to write READMEs (Week 2, subtasks 1.4-1.9)

**Contains:**
- ORGAN-I (Theory) template — 3,000+ words expected
- ORGAN-II (Art) template — 2,500+ words + demos
- ORGAN-III (Commerce) template — 2,000+ words + metrics
- ORGAN-IV (Orchestration) template — Governance-focused
- ORGAN-V (Public) template — Publishing-focused
- ORGAN-VI (Community) template — Participation-focused
- ORGAN-VII (Marketing) template — Strategy-focused

Each template includes:
- Section headings (use as-is)
- Instructions in [brackets]
- Expected length + time per repo
- What to customize

**Time to read:** 30 minutes (browse relevant templates)  
**Use while:** Writing each README (copy template → customize → commit)

**Action items:**
1. Choose template matching your repo's organ
2. Copy template verbatim
3. Replace [bracketed instructions] with your content
4. Don't skip sections
5. Customize examples to your repo
6. Test code examples before committing

---

### 04-per-organ-validation-checklists.md (QA Process)

**What it is:** Detailed checklist for peer-reviewing each README before commit

**Read this if:** You're doing peer review (Week 2, throughout, especially day 4-5)

**Contains:**
- ORGAN-I validation checklist (8 checks × 10 repos)
- ORGAN-II validation checklist (9 checks × 13 repos)
- ORGAN-III validation checklist (8 checks × 12 repos)
- ORGAN-IV validation checklist (5 checks × 3 repos)
- ORGAN-V validation checklist (5 checks × 1 repo)
- ORGAN-VI validation checklist (4 checks × 2 repos)
- ORGAN-VII validation checklist (4 checks × 3 repos)
- Peer review process (how to review + red flags)

Each checklist includes:
- Content completeness ✓
- Accuracy & clarity ✓
- Portfolio relevance ✓
- Link validation ✓
- Ready-to-launch criteria

**Time to read:** 20 minutes (skim, then reference)  
**Use while:** Peer-reviewing READMEs

**Action items:**
1. Use checklist during peer review (don't skip items)
2. Provide feedback to author (use checklist language)
3. Mark readme complete only after all boxes checked
4. Flag red flags immediately (broken links, non-working code)
5. Don't commit incomplete READMEs

---

### 05-risk-map-and-sequencing.md (Dependencies + Risks)

**What it is:** Dependency analysis, critical path, risks, and optimal sequencing

**Read this if:** You want to understand what can go wrong + optimal order to prevent it

**Contains:**
- Dependency map (which repos block which?)
- Critical path (fastest route to completion)
- Risk assessment (7 major risks + mitigation)
- Optimal sequencing (what to do each day to finish)
- What can go wrong (5 detailed scenarios)
- Go/No-Go decision gates (Friday EOD, Wednesday mid-week, Sunday final)
- Contingency timeline (if schedule slips)

**Time to read:** 30 minutes  
**Reference while:** Executing Phase 1 (use for daily planning)

**Action items:**
1. Understand critical dependencies (don't break them)
2. Use optimal sequencing as Week 2 daily plan
3. Check go/no-go gates on Friday (week 1), Wednesday (mid-week 2), Sunday (final)
4. If schedule slips, adjust per contingency plans (don't panic)
5. Escalate issues early if 15+ hours behind

---

## How to Use These 6 Documents

### Week 1 (Planning Phase)

**Monday-Thursday (Feb 10-13):**
1. Read 00-c-master-summary.md completely (30 min)
2. Make 3 strategic decisions + record in registry (4 hours)
3. Read 01-readme-audit-framework.md (20 min)
4. Read 02-repo-inventory-audit.md (20 min)
5. Skim 03-per-organ-readme-templates.md (30 min)
6. Create task list from Document 02 (assign repos to people)
7. Print out 04-per-organ-validation-checklists.md (for Week 2 reference)

**Friday (Feb 14):**
1. Read 05-risk-map-and-sequencing.md (30 min)
2. Check go/no-go gate: Are we ready for Week 2?
3. If yes: Confirm Week 2 assignments + start dates
4. If no: Fix blockers + retry gate

**Total Week 1 reading time:** ~3 hours  
**Total Week 1 preparation:** ~15-20 hours  
**Week 1 complete:** All templates created + all repos audited + task list ready

### Week 2 (Execution Phase)

**Every day (Mon-Sun):**
1. Follow daily plan from Document 05 (Risk Map section: "Optimal Sequencing")
2. Each author: Write README using Document 03 template
3. Each peer: Review README using Document 04 checklist
4. Daily progress: Track how many repos complete (target: 8-10 per day)

**Critical checkpoints:**
- **Wednesday (Feb 19):** Mid-week check: Am I on track? (Use Document 05 gate)
- **Friday (Feb 21):** Week 2 mid-point: Portfolio infrastructure done?
- **Sunday (Feb 23):** Final go/no-go: Phase 1 complete?

**Total Week 2 reading time:** ~0 hours (reference only)  
**Total Week 2 execution:** ~50 hours (write + review + validate)  
**Week 2 complete:** All 60 repos documented + peer-reviewed + links validated

- [ ] All 60 repos have comprehensive README

- [ ] All external links validated (no 404s)

- [ ] repo-registry.json updated with documentation status
- [ ] Personal account consolidation complete
- [ ] Empty/skeleton repo decisions executed

- [ ] Phase 2 ready to begin

**If any criterion incomplete:** Phase 1 extends until complete. Don't move to Phase 2 with partial documentation.

## Questions? FAQ

**Q: Can I do this solo or do I need a team?**  
A: Solo is fine (70 hours over 2 weeks = ~5 hours/day). With team, assign repos by organ + parallelize.

**Q: What if I get stuck on a particular README?**  
A: Use template (Document 03) + checklist (Document 04). If still stuck, move to next repo + return later.

**Q: Do all READMEs really need to be 3,000+ words?**  
A: No. Minimums: ORGAN-I (3,000), ORGAN-II (2,500), ORGAN-III (2,000), others (1,500+). Quality over quantity.

**Q: What if I discover a repo shouldn't be public?**  
A: Move to private + update registry. Don't delay; fix immediately.

**Q: Can I start Phase 2 with Phase 1 incomplete?**  
A: No. Phase 2 depends on all 60 repos documented. Complete Phase 1 first.

**Q: What if I miss the Feb 23 deadline?**  
A: No problem. Extend to Mar 2 (1 week slip). Better late + complete than rushed + incomplete.
```
